UNRRA Announces Partial Lifting of Suspension Order on Relief Supplies to China; Ships Will Depart for China After Resolution of US Labor Strike

[United Press, Washington, 21st] LaGuardia, Director-General of UNRRA, announced today: "The suspension of UNRRA's relief supplies to China has been partially lifted." LaGuardia stated: "Chinese ports that can handle relief supplies can request these supplies and they will be shipped." LaGuardia's announcement stated: "The speed of distribution of supplies in Chinese ports has greatly improved... The embargo on supplies to China is hereby lifted, and supplies will be shipped out according to the capacity of Chinese ports, upon request of the respective ports." LaGuardia said: "Ships will depart as soon as the current labor strike is resolved." He also said that the report on the improved speed of distribution of supplies in Chinese ports came from Major General Edgerton, Director of UNRRA's China Office. The announcement was only seventy-three words long and did not explain the detailed plan.

[Our City News] A spokesman for the Chinese National Relief and Rehabilitation Administration (CNRRA) recently issued a statement on the UNRRA Director-General LaGuardia's announcement of the partial lifting of the suspension order on supplies to China, saying: "The UNRRA's announcement of the partial lifting of the suspension order is the result of months of continuous efforts by this Administration to clear out supplies." "In terms of the current distribution of supplies by this Administration, UNRRA urgently needs to fully resume the transportation of supplies to China, otherwise it will be difficult to coordinate with the future work of this Administration." It also said: "Since UNRRA announced the suspension order in July of this year, the quantity of supplies distributed by this Administration to various places has increased significantly each month. In July, this Administration shipped 45,000 tons of supplies to other ports, which increased to 68,000 tons in August, and 96,000 tons in September, totaling 120,000 tons including supplies distributed in Shanghai." "This Administration's distribution of supplies is constantly increasing, but UNRRA's transportation has been slow. Taking the recent week of October 5th to 11th as an example, this Administration distributed and shipped a total of 21,958 tons of supplies in Shanghai and to other ports. During the same week, only 14,683 tons of UNRRA supplies were unloaded in Shanghai." "Currently, there are still 115,000 tons of supplies in Shanghai warehouses, of which 65,000 tons need to be processed and modified in Shanghai, so only 50,000 tons of supplies can be shipped to other ports for distribution. Adding the 50,000 tons that UNRRA is scheduled to ship to China in the next two months, the total is only 100,000 tons. During the same period, this Administration's transportation volume can reach 240,000 tons." "I once consulted experts on UNRRA's resumption of transportation, and they all said that even if UNRRA immediately implements a full resumption of transportation, it will take three months to see results."

[Our City News] According to the China News Agency's Eastern Dispatch: Recently, 28 UNRRA giant ships, fully loaded with supplies, are sailing to Shanghai and will arrive soon.

British Communist Party Member of Parliament Inquires in the House of Commons About UNRRA's Relief Plan for China

[Reuters, London, 21st] Labor Party Member of Parliament Williams inquired in the House of Commons: "After UNRRA ceases its activities, what is the plan for relief work in China? What agency will take over this work? How will the experience of UNRRA's work in China be considered, so that past mistakes are not repeated?" Undersecretary McNeil replied: "UNRRA's plan in China will not be completed until the fall of 1947 at the earliest. In August, the UNRRA General Assembly held in Geneva passed a resolution to submit the question of whether countries still need relief after UNRRA ceases its work to the United Nations General Assembly for discussion. Therefore, the General Assembly should decide how to handle relief work. Before making a decision, it should first examine whether the countries still need external assistance in addition to loans from international banks. This question is related to the balance of payments of the countries and cannot be accurately estimated in advance, nor is it within the scope of UNRRA's post-disaster relief." "As for the experience gained by UNRRA, it should be provided to any agency that undertakes relief work in China. It is reported that UNRRA has set up a commissioner to record the activities in China in detail, which will be a very valuable record."

He Fengshan Reports on Overseas Chinese Affairs: Rice Has Been Allocated to Aid Refugees Who Escaped from the Dutch East Indies; Overseas Chinese Who Illegally Entered the Philippines Have Been Properly Sent Back to China

[Central News Agency, Nanjing, 22nd] In order to understand the recent situation of our country's protection of overseas Chinese, the reporter specially visited the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. He Fengshan, Director of the Information Department of the Ministry, received the reporter and answered the questions as follows:

(Question) It was reported a few days ago that more than 2,000 overseas Chinese, fleeing from the disaster-stricken area of the Dutch East Indies near Panipagan, sought refuge on Gedang Island in British Malaya, and Consul Xu Menghong, stationed in Kuala Lumpur, discussed relief matters. How is this matter progressing? (Answer) When Consul Xu learned that the aforementioned refugees had arrived on Gedang Island under his jurisdiction, he requested 600 dan (石) of low-priced rice from the local government for relief. Although the supply of rice in Malaya is currently very difficult, with the assistance of the provincial governor, the welfare department has allocated the full amount for emergency use. Consul Xu is now trying to transport another 50 tons of rice to Bagan Siapiapi in Sumatra to relieve the refugees there, and is contacting overseas Chinese groups to launch fundraising for disaster relief.

(Question) It is rumored that dozens of overseas Chinese were arrested by the Philippine authorities for illegal entry. What is the process and how did our government handle it? (Answer) Recently, more than 60 people from southern Fujian took two steamships and sailed from Taiwan to northern Luzon, illegally entering the country. They were all captured by the Philippine Constabulary and escorted to Manila. After receiving the report, we have asked the Philippine authorities to properly send them back to China. After investigation, it was found that these two groups of passengers were deceived. The shipowners have offices in Xiamen and Taiwan, advertising to recruit passengers, claiming to send them to the Philippines for 150,000 yuan per person, which led to the passengers being deceived and suffering mental and financial losses, and affecting the long-standing reputation of our overseas Chinese in the Philippines. Now the Ministry has consulted with relevant agencies to severely punish the shipowners.

[Central News Agency, Hong Kong, 21st] 1,700 overseas Chinese repatriated from Java have submitted a petition to Guo Dehua, the special envoy of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for Guangdong and Guangxi, for forwarding to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The content is unknown, but it is believed to be an appeal for the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to assist.

[Reuters, Nanjing, 22nd] Bartholomew, who has been the British Air Force Attaché in China since 1943, is scheduled to return home on the 23rd. The post of Attaché will be taken over by Haskins. Haskins is a famous British Air Force general. On the eve of the outbreak of the European War, he led the 150th Squadron to France. He later participated in the Burma Campaign. After Yang Huilan, the chairman, gave a brief opening speech, Ms. Hu Yiru delivered a welcome speech, hoping that Mrs. Cripps' visit would further enhance the connection between Chinese and British women and promote friendship between the two countries in order to strive for world peace and construction. Mrs. Cripps introduced Ms. Miller, Secretary of the United Aid to China Fund (UACF), to report on the organization and work of the UACF, and hoped to build a Chinese Building in London in the future as a center to promote Chinese-British friendship and communicate the culture of the two countries. She then said: "Although women's rights are developed in the UK, there are no female judges, but China already has a female judge surnamed Li, whom I met in Chongqing this time, which shows that the Chinese women's movement is not lagging behind." (Central News Agency note: There is more than one female judge in our country.) The attending representatives then presented Mrs. Cripps with an autographed commemorative album, followed by refreshments and adjournment.

[Central News Agency, Chengdu, 22nd] Mrs. Cripps left Chengdu by special train at 9:30 am today to go to Guanxian. She visited the Dujiangyan irrigation project and arrived in Guanxian at 12 noon. She returned to Chengdu from Guanxian at 2 pm and arrived at 4:15 pm. Mrs. Cripps is scheduled to fly to Lanzhou by special plane on the 23rd and will go to Zhangye and Shandan, where there is a Peili Middle School funded by the United Aid to China Fund. Later, she will visit Yan'an, Zhengzhou, Beiping and other places.

The Destruction of the Pingsui Railway by the Communist Army (Secretly photographed by Li Hua of CNRRA)

Academia Sinica Council Meeting Discusses Work Guidelines; Passes "Academician" Title and Stipulates Quotas

[Central News Agency, Nanjing, 22nd] The second session of the third annual meeting of the Academia Sinica Council was held in the auditorium of the Academia Sinica on the 22nd. Twenty-eight council members, including Zhu Jiahua, Wang Shijie, Weng Wenhao, Bingzhi, Hu Shi, and Fu Sinian, attended the meeting. The meeting was chaired by Zhu Jiahua, the chairman of the council. The general work guidelines and the allocation of funds were discussed. Wu Youxun, Hu Shi, and Fu Sinian believed that the Academia Sinica had not yet achieved the ideal in terms of the concentration of talent. Mao Yisheng said: "The Academia Sinica itself is a research institution. On the one hand, it should enrich research work. On the other hand, it should be responsible for guiding the research work of academic institutions across the country." Hu Shi also suggested merging research institutes with similar properties to reduce units, concentrate manpower, and make it easier to show work performance. After the break, the meeting was resumed to review the work reports of the research institutes. In order to save time, Fu Sinian, Wu Youxun, Zhu Jingxi, Hu Xianqin, Mao Yisheng, Li Shuhua, and Zhu Kezhen were selected as members of the committee, with Fu Sinian as the convener. The meeting was adjourned at 12 noon. The meeting was held at 3 pm to discuss "the proposal to stipulate the name, establishment, election and related matters of Member acadimia sinica". Regarding the name of Member of acadima sinica, the council members expressed their opinions, including "Academician", "Yuan Ru (院儒)", "Yuan Lü (院侶)", "Yuan Zheng (院正)", "Yuan Yuan (院員)", and "Member", etc. As a result, the name "Academician" was passed, because among the 22 council members present at that time, 13 people expressed their support for using it. Another important proposal: "Please set up the Academician of the Academia Sinica and revise the organization and mission of the Council", it was decided that the quota of academicians will be 80 to 100 people in the first phase, and up to 10 people will be elected each year thereafter. In the future, the Council will be formed by the election of council members from the academicians. This resolution has been formed into a review committee by Hu Shi, Fu Sinian, Li Shuhua, Wu Youxun, Sa Bendong, Bing Zhi, and Chen Heng, and Hu Shi was elected as the convener.

[Our Newspaper Nanjing Dispatch, 22nd] The annual meeting of the Academia Sinica Council will hold a group review meeting on the morning of the 23rd. The first group will review the work reports of the research institutes, and the second group will discuss the establishment, election and related matters of academicians. A plenary meeting will be held in the afternoon.

Agricultural Loans in Recovered Areas Have Reached 1 Billion Yuan

[Our Newspaper Nanjing Dispatch, 22nd] In order to assist farmers in the recovered areas to quickly resume production, the Four Banks Joint Office formulated the Implementation Measures for Emergency Relief Agricultural Loans in Recovered Areas after the victory of the Anti-Japanese War, and submitted it to the Executive Yuan. The National Treasury allocated 4 billion yuan to the Farmers Bank of China for lending, including 1 billion yuan for the first and second phases and 2 billion yuan for the third phase. Later, due to the particularly heavy disaster in Hunan Province, it was specially requested that the National Treasury allocate 1 billion yuan to the Farmers Bank of China for lending. As of the end of August this year, the bank had lent out a cumulative amount of more than 1 billion and 9 million yuan in the recovered areas of 13 provinces, including Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, and Guangdong. A total of 5,900 organizations and more than 420,000 farmers borrowed money, which has been quite effective in relieving farmers and restoring agriculture. The bank is still continuing to quickly approve the remaining amount of the loan.

Restoration Work of the Palace Museum is Not Yet Completed

Ma Heng Talks in Nanjing

[Central News Agency, Nanjing, 22nd] Ma Heng, Director of the National Palace Museum, came to Nanjing to attend the board meeting of the Palace Museum. The reporter specially interviewed him. He said: "The restoration work of the Palace Museum has not yet been completed. In Beiping, the museum received the bronze collection of German expatriate Yang Ningshi. The oldest items are from the Shang Dynasty, and there are also unearthed objects from Anyang, Henan. Before the war, the excavation work in Anyang was the responsibility of the Academia Sinica. After the outbreak of the Anti-Japanese War, Anyang fell into the hands of the enemy. The people excavated on their own. Occasionally, they would take the findings to Beiping for sale, all of which were collected by Yang Ningshi. Therefore, both the quantity and quality are very impressive. In addition, Guo Shiwu, a porcelain collector in Beiping, who was also the designer of the Hongxian Kiln during the Yuan Shikai era, left a will when he passed away, wishing to donate his entire collection to the National Government. At that time, the enemy and puppets tried every means to seize it, but Guo's descendants preserved it until today, which was not easy. After the recovery, it was received by the Palace Museum. The museum has set up special rooms to display these bronzes and porcelains, which will be open to the public from October 10th." When asked about the relics of Luo Zhenyu of the puppet Manchukuo government, Ma said: "Luo had sent all his collections to the puppet Zhangchun Museum before his death, and the books were stored in Luo's residence in Lushun. They were all lost when the Soviet army entered the Northeast, which is a pity."

Ministry of National Defense Military Law Department Executes Three Military Criminals; Two are Traitors and One Embezzled Public Property

[Central News Agency, Nanjing, 22nd] The Military Law Department of the Ministry of National Defense executed two military traitors, Li Ou Yi and Dong Xiutian, and a military officer, Wang Zhongmin, who embezzled public property. Li Ou Yi was originally a major general staff officer of the 5th Guerrilla Area Command in Guangdong. In November of the 28th year of the Republic of China, he was summoned to Nanjing by the enemy and successively served as the education director of the Guangzhou branch of the puppet Central Military Academy, and the lieutenant general director of the puppet Military Affairs Commission's office, and the commander of the puppet capital garrison and concurrently the police chief. Dong Xiutian once served as the company commander of the 735th regiment of the 45th brigade of the army. In October of the 27th year of the Republic of China, he was captured by the enemy and puppets in Suzhou, and then served the enemy, successively serving as the captain, battalion commander, adjutant, and regimental commander of the 1st and 2nd District Command of the puppet Zhejiang Pacification. Wang Zhongmin was the colonel warehouse director of the 33rd warehouse of the former Ministry of Military and Political Affairs in Suzhou. In March and April of this year, he took the liberty of handing over 109 bags of white sugar (each bag weighing 150 kilograms) stored in the warehouse to Fu Ziben, the captain adjutant of the Suzhou POW Management Office of the Third Theater Command, who introduced it to the merchant Wang Mingjie, and obtained more than 6 million yuan, which was divided for spending. The matter was discovered by the former Ministry of Military and Political Affairs, and Wang Zhongmin and Fu Ziben were detained and interrogated. After interrogating and confirming that the above was true, Wang Zhongmin was sentenced to death for embezzling public property, and Fu Ziben was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment and four years of deprivation of civil rights for helping others to embezzle public property.

Editorial

Wishing the United Nations General Assembly Success

The United Nations General Assembly opens in New York today. Politicians and diplomats from fifty-one countries around the world are gathering together to begin the arduous task of discussing how to create world peace. The eyes of all humanity are focused on New York, closely watching the development of this international conference. Although most observers still hold a pessimistic view of the future of the United Nations General Assembly, the desire of people in all countries for world peace is so urgent today that as long as there is a glimmer of hope, they ultimately feel that there is a possibility of a breakthrough and will never give up hope. People in all countries still have unlimited expectations for the success of the United Nations General Assembly, so U.S. Undersecretary of State Acheson, on the eve of the United Nations General Assembly, addressed the delegates of various countries and said very frankly: "The United States has consistently supported the United Nations as its foreign policy; and will continue to boldly move forward and continue to adopt this policy without discouragement. The United States government firmly believes that the United Nations will make full progress on the difficult long road and complete world peace." Although these are diplomatic pleasantries from American diplomats, they are enough to increase the confidence of delegates from various countries that the United Nations General Assembly will be successful.

Today, the center of gravity of the world political situation is undoubtedly completely on the relationship between the United States and the Soviet Union. The key to the success or failure of the United Nations General Assembly also lies here. U.S. Secretary of State Byrnes, who had just returned from Paris, declared when reporting to the people of the country on the proceedings of the Twenty-One Nation Peace Conference: "The most worrying aspect of the current situation is that the tension between the United States and the Soviet Union is increasing rather than decreasing, and the United States has reached the end of its concessions to the Soviet Union." However, Soviet Foreign Minister Molotov, after arriving in New York, issued a statement to the American press saying: "I believe that sincerity and goodwill will certainly lead to mutual understanding; therefore, I also believe that the work facing this United Nations General Assembly will be completed, and any difficulties can be solved easily. The Soviet delegation will be able to contribute to this United Nations General Assembly and the Foreign Ministers' Meeting to be held in early November, so that it can complete its work to promote peace and the well-being of people of all countries, large and small, around the world." Although these are diplomatic pleasantries, they are enough to make the world increasingly hopeful that the relationship between the United States and the Soviet Union will improve. Therefore, on the eve of the opening of the United Nations General Assembly, we saw New York filled with an atmosphere of peace and brightness, which is really gratifying, and we hope that the world situation will be brighter from now on and that the world's yearning for peace will not be in vain.

Since we are in this kind of international atmosphere, we should naturally welcome the opening of the United Nations General Assembly with a happy mood and sincerely wish the United Nations General Assembly success. However, looking back on the past and looking forward to the future, after making a comprehensive analysis of the current international situation, we ultimately feel that the future of the United Nations General Assembly is not to be taken too optimistically and that great wise and benevolent politicians from various countries still need to work hard to overcome all difficulties and pave a broad road for world peace. Based on what we have seen, we would like to offer a word to politicians and diplomats from various countries.

First, when we recall the international situation over the past year and a half, we have only seen one disturbance after another, and several basic issues have gone in a big circle and returned to their original starting points without any resolution. This is really the most discouraging phenomenon after the war. In Europe, it has been a year and a half since Nazi Germany unconditionally surrendered and the war ended. In the Far East, it has been more than a year since Japan surrendered. During this period, many politicians and diplomats have tried their best to work for peace, but true peace has not yet come to the world. Internationally, there have been meetings of the five foreign ministers, meetings of the three foreign ministers, the United Nations General Assembly, the meetings of the four foreign ministers, and then from the meetings of the four foreign ministers to the Paris Peace Conference, and now it will be from the United Nations General Assembly to the meetings of the four foreign ministers. The number of international conferences has created an unprecedented record in human history, but what are the results of these international conferences? Let's make a total settlement. The only achievement is the five peace proposals passed by the Paris Peace Conference. Other important issues could not be resolved by the Foreign Ministers' Meeting, so they were transferred to the Paris Peace Conference for handling, but the Paris Peace Conference still failed to reach a resolution, and now they have been returned to the Foreign Ministers' Meeting for discussion. This cruel fact gives us a valuable lesson, that is, creating peace is not easy and requires the cooperation of all countries to have hope of success.

Second, when we study the reasons for the slow progress of peace work, we cannot but attribute it to the fact that the great powers cannot treat each other with sincerity, which leads to mutual suspicion and the emergence of two opposing worlds. In fact, the Soviet Union needs peace and does not want to see war again; the United States also needs peace and hates war; since the goals of both sides are the same, why can't they cooperate in international conferences? This is obviously due to mutual suspicion between the two sides. There is a saying in Chinese: "Without sincerity, there is nothing." Since the United States and the Soviet Union cannot treat each other with sincerity, no problem can be solved. On the contrary, if both sides can be open and honest, nothing is unspeakable, and any difficulty can be easily solved; as the saying goes, "Where sincerity reaches, metal and stone are opened." Foreign Minister Molotov also said this in his speech in New York, which makes us believe that delegates from all countries, especially the United States and the Soviet Union, will be able to treat each other with sincerity in this United Nations General Assembly, abandon all differences in opinions, and reach a completely unanimous agreement.

Third, because we hope that the United Nations General Assembly can be successful, we must point out the defects in the United Nations organization, that is, it lacks democratic spirit in its organization. The post-war world has already entered a new era of peace and democracy, and the present can be regarded as a democratic century. People in all countries of the world not only demand the democratization of domestic politics, but also demand the democratization of international politics. The politics of power has become a historical relic and should not be allowed to revive and reappear on the international stage of the democratic century. After carefully studying the United Nations Charter, we can know that the organization of the United Nations General Assembly that opens today has very undemocratic aspects. In its theory, all countries of the United Nations, regardless of size or strength, are equal in law and completely equal. However, in the Security Council, there is a distinction between permanent members and non-permanent members, and permanent members have the privilege of exercising the veto power over the resolutions passed by the Security Council. Any resolution that is approved by all countries cannot be established as long as one major power (permanent member) expresses dissent. What an undemocratic system this is! Therefore, if we want to hope that the United Nations General Assembly can be successful and that it can become the only effective tool for maintaining world peace, then the veto power must be abolished. There has long been such a movement in the United States, and it has been advocated to all countries in the world, and all countries have expressed their approval. The only country that has expressed opposition is the Soviet Union alone. Before the relationship between the United States and the Soviet Union has improved, the Soviet Union alone holds a dissenting opinion. From the standpoint of the Soviet Union, it naturally has its reasons, but when all countries treat each other with sincerity and no longer have fears, the Soviet Union naturally has no reason to insist that the United Nations organization still retain its fatal wound.

In short, the issues discussed at this United Nations General Assembly, in addition to current international disputes, will also discuss various issues that are beneficial to human welfare. It has a very close relationship to the future of all mankind. Therefore, for the benefit of all countries, and also for the future of the world, this conference is only allowed to succeed and not allowed to fail. Let us wish the United Nations General Assembly success here.

Bizarre Bloodshed in Wuchang District Court Holding Room: Yuan Hongsheng's Throat Suddenly Slit Open

[Report from our Hankou office on the 22nd] A bizarre bloodshed case occurred in the holding room of the Wuchang District Court yesterday afternoon. The victim, Yuan Hongsheng, had his throat slit open and was bleeding profusely. He immediately fainted and has been sent to the Provincial Hospital for emergency treatment by court officials. His condition is still critical. According to a subsequent investigation, the victim, Yuan, was being tried in court on suspicion of treason. Later, due to insufficient evidence, he was released on bail. Yesterday afternoon, Yuan invited local Baojia gentry to prove his behavior during the occupation. The court first questioned the Baojia gentry, while Yuan waited alone in the holding room. There was originally no one else in the room, but when the bailiff returned to summon him, he found Yuan in a terrible state. Everyone who heard about it was shocked. A search was conducted in the room, but no murder weapon was left behind. It was obviously a case of assassination, and the court is strictly pursuing the murderer.

Page 3

Major Overhaul of Tax Collection in Zhejiang Province; Security Forces Must Complete Reorganization by the End of the Month

[Report from our Hangzhou office] The finances of Zhejiang Province are in dire straits. It is estimated that the deficit for the second half of this year will reach 27.2 billion. The provincial government can only make up for this huge deficit by reorganizing tax collection. The measures are divided into two categories: A: Reorganizing existing taxes: (1) Business tax: Conduct thorough and comprehensive investigations to strictly prevent concealment, and actively collect business tax from the grain and transportation industries in accordance with the orders of the Ministry of Finance. (2) Land tax: Reassess land prices in accordance with the law and collect the full amount. (3) Deed tax: Conduct earnest investigations to clear up white deeds and make realistic evaluations. (4) Slaughter tax: Conduct strict inspections and prevent illegal slaughter, and collect taxes directly on a per-head basis according to current market prices. (5) Business license tax: Should be closely coordinated with business tax for earnest inspection and collection. (6) Usage license tax: Vehicles, ships, sedan chairs, etc., should all be inspected and collected in accordance with regulations. (7) Feast tax: Earnestly promote the use of donation tickets instead of bills and send personnel to conduct strict spot checks. (8) Entertainment tax: In addition to conducting earnest inspections and collections in accordance with the law, tea houses with entertainment facilities should also be taxed. (9) Housing police donation: In addition to conducting earnest compilation and inspection in accordance with the law, police authorities should assist in compilation and collection. B: Collect taxes that are appropriate to local conditions: Under the principle of not conflicting with central laws and regulations, counties are allowed to collect taxes that are appropriate to local conditions, the methods of which must be approved by popular opinion institutions and approved by the provincial government for filing with the Ministry.

[Report from our Hangzhou office] The Zhejiang Provincial Security Forces have been ordered to implement reorganization, which has already begun and must be completed and reported by the end of this month. The main points are as follows: (1) The original Security Regiments 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5 will be reorganized into five general detachments, each with three battalions, and each battalion with four companies. (2) The original Security Independent Detachments 1 and 2, Special Service Battalion 1, Communications Battalion, Independent Battalion 2, and Rotation Company will have their designations revoked. (3) The aforementioned units will be merged into one battalion and placed under the command of the general detachment. (4) The original Special Service Battalion 2 will be reorganized into an independent battalion. (5) Surplus personnel must report to the Security Headquarters for orders before November 15.

(2) Establish an association in Nanjing to facilitate contact between Jiangsu representatives and exchange opinions. (3) Elect Wang Baoxuan, Niu Changyao, Zhao Yiqing, Yan Huizi, Wang Liangzhong, and Ling Shaozu to raise 30 million yuan in funds. (4) Establish four groups: documentation, administration, liaison, and research, with each representative voluntarily joining one group. Bao Mingshu was elected as the convener of the documentation group, Niu Changyao as the convener of the administration group, Xiang Jutan as the convener of the liaison group, and Ni Bi as the convener of the research group. (5) As the counties in northern Jiangsu are gradually recovered, all issues related to land, security, and economy in each county will be studied separately by the research group and suggestions will be made to the provincial government. (6) Send a letter to the provincial government to forward to the central government a request to temporarily suspend conscription in the recovered areas of northern Jiangsu. (7) Send a letter to the provincial government requesting prompt subsidies for Baojia expenses in the recovered and unrecovered areas of northern Jiangsu. (8) The Xu prefectural counties in the recovered areas of northern Jiangsu are in dire need of wheat seeds and agricultural implements. It is recommended that the provincial government order the Agricultural Bank to quickly prepare seed and oxen loans and request the Su-Ning branch office to allocate 100 tractors and 100 sets of attached plows and harrows to be distributed to each county to assist in the restoration of rural areas.

Suzhou Repairs Confucian Temple; Plans to Establish Literature Museum

[Report from our Suzhou office] The Kunshan County Confucian Temple Restoration Committee believes that the county's Confucian Temple was severely damaged by the enemy during the War of Resistance, with the halls and buildings almost completely destroyed. After the victory, local people proposed the idea of ​​repairing it, but because the passing troops were living inside, it was impossible to start construction. Recently, the county temporary council sent a letter to the county government, requesting that the competent authorities order the troops to move out. Repairs should be carried out as soon as possible to protect the relics of the former sages. Therefore, on the 19th, representatives from relevant agencies and local elders were invited to the Minglun Hall of the Fuxue to hold the first meeting to discuss the repair plan. The following resolutions were made: (1) The repair funds will be budgeted by the committee, and the county government will be requested to allocate them from the surplus items in the 35th fiscal year. The Wuxian Post-War Relief Association will be requested to ask the Su-Ning branch office to provide work relief for repairs. The estimate should include the repair project of the Dacheng Hall and the East Worshipping Hall, and the Construction Section will be requested to re-estimate. (2) A Wuxian Literature Museum will be established. Jiang Yinqiu, Gu Jiegang, Wang Zhijiu, Fan Junbo, and Zhang Shoupeng will be appointed as design committee members, and Jiang Yinqiu will be publicly elected as convener. (3) A portion of the vacant land will be designated for merchants to contract for the operation of flower gardens or nurseries. (4) Wang Diancun, Zhang Boyin, and Jin Songcen will be added as committee members.

Pinghu Merges Townships

[Report from our Pinghu office] Regarding the merger of townships in this county, the provincial order was previously received, and the entire county was reduced to 26 townships based on geography, history, customs, and wealth. The county government had just convened a meeting to complete the adjustment. Later, the Tenth District Commissioner's Office ordered that it be reduced to 19 townships, causing the previous resolution to be completely overturned. The county government then reconvened a group meeting to review and approve it. According to the former administrative districts, it was divided into five townships in the urban area, five townships in the Zhapu area, five townships in the Xincang area, and four townships in the Xindi area. The principles will be submitted to the County Council for review shortly, and all mergers can be completed in mid-November.

Jiangsu Provincial Agricultural Products Exhibition; Soliciting Products from Various Counties

[Zhenjiang] The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction believes that the province has a large variety of famous local products. In order to encourage improvement and increased production, it plans to collect products from various places and display them in a special room for observation and research. It has ordered the counties under its jurisdiction to quickly make specimens of various special products from agriculture, industry, commerce, and mining within their borders and send them to the department for exhibition.

Traitorous Township Chief's Heinous Crimes; Shi Guanggen Sentenced to Death; Evidence Collected in Suzhou for the Changshu Japanese Military Police Massacre

[Report from our Suzhou on the 22nd] The case in which the High Court sentenced a traitor to death on the 22nd involved Shi Guanggen, who served as a puppet township chief in Bupu Township, Chetai County during the war. During his tenure, he committed all kinds of crimes, including kidnapping and extortion, and had many blood debts. From April to July of the 32nd year of the Republic, he repeatedly arrested Wang Xiaoqin, the principal of the township's primary school, twice, extorting a total of 53,000 yuan. Fearing retaliation, he killed Wang on the evening of July 3 of the same year. After the victory, Wang's family and other victims reported him. After the Suzhou High Court concluded its trial, it ruled that although Shi was only a puppet township chief, his crimes were heinous. In addition to sentencing him to death to uphold the law, all of his property was confiscated.

[Report from our Suzhou on the 22nd] Lu Qi, a judge of the First Pacification Zone Military Court, arrived in Suzhou from Yu on the morning of the 22nd and went directly to the Suzhou High Court to meet with President Sun to discuss matters. At 4:00 PM, he was accompanied by officials from the High Court to the detention center to interrogate Lu Shihua and Zheng Fengshi, two enemy military police from Changshu and Taicang. All personnel were excused during the interrogation, and the case seemed to be quite important. The interrogation lasted for more than an hour. Reporters later learned that Lu's trip was to collect evidence for the massacre case by enemy military police officer Haruki Yonemura.

Enemy-Controlled Wang Yiqing Arrested in Xincang

[Report from our Pinghu office] Wang Yiqing, the murderous demon who ran rampant on the border between Jiangsu and Zhejiang during the enemy puppet era, was captured by the criminal police team near the Xinmiao Temple in Xincang Town on the evening of the 18th. He was escorted to the county police station overnight for questioning and sent to the Zhejiang Security Headquarters in Hangzhou on the 21st for handling according to law. After the county fell, Wang rebelled and served in the Ninth Branch of the Loyalty and Salvation Army. He was later captured by Japanese bandits and joined the Special Service Corps of the Puppet Four Provinces Administration Camp in Hangzhou, serving as the captain of the First Battalion. In the 33rd year of the Republic, he was transferred to the Songjiang Military Police Special Operations Team as a secret agent. After the victory, he hid in Suzhou. Recently, he returned to [Blank], hid weapons, and attempted to conduct activities again. Someone secretly informed the Provincial Security Headquarters, which secretly ordered this county to investigate. The dragnet of justice is inescapable.

Ships Start Sailing from Bengbu to Zhengyangguan

[Report from our Zhengyangguan office] In order to strengthen the transport of goods between Bengbu and Zhengyang and to facilitate the travel of merchants, the Changhuai Shipping Company ticket office began operating shipping services on the 15th. Ships depart from Zhengyangguan to Bengbu on odd-numbered days and from Bengbu to Zhengyangguan on even-numbered days, arriving on the same day.

Changyin Sand Fully Launches Suppression; Another Bandit Leader in Yangcheng District Killed

[Report from our Changshu office] Changyin Sand originally belonged to the three counties of Yu, Tong, and Cheng. After the provincial government ordered it to be placed under the jurisdiction of Changshu, the Tong County side has not yet handed it over. It is learned that the suppression work will not be delayed as a result and will be implemented quickly. Commander Kong of the Jiangyin Fortress and County Magistrate Pan here will serve as the chief and deputy commanders, respectively. All steps have been arranged. Commander Kong arrived in Yu on the 20th. Chief of Staff Nie Qi and military judge Mao Xueqin came with him. On the 21st, they went to Changyin Sand with County Magistrate Pan, parachute battalion commander Guo, and others to inspect and carry out their mission in order to complete it as scheduled.

[Report from our Suzhou office] The Yangcheng District Suppression Headquarters reported at around 4:00 PM on the 20th that Qiu Yingqi's troops of the 15th Platoon of the Third Battalion of the Parachute Regiment stationed in Xicang Town, Xishan County, had escorted bandits Qian Xiaodi and Gao Xiaodi, as well as four seized short guns, to Suzhou. As the reporter happened to be interviewing at the headquarters, he learned the details, which are recorded as follows: At around 10:00 AM on the 14th of this month, an incident occurred in Dongjing Bridge in which bandits used weapons to rob the shipping vessel between Suzhou and Ganlu. The 6th Platoon of the Parachute Regiment stationed in Ganlu learned of the incident and set out to search the next day, and contacted and coordinated with the 15th Platoon stationed in Xicang to surround and suppress the bandits. As expected, bandit traces were found in Xinnan Township, and they rushed to arrest them. Bandit leader Li Zaiyang led his troops Mei Baoquan, Gao Jinbao, Qian Xiaodi, Gao Xiaodi, and others and took the lead in firing their weapons and resisting arrest, leading to a fierce battle. Bullets flew like strings of beads, and the two sides made contact for a long time. The bandits retreated when their ammunition ran out. They were pursued to Taofandian Township, where bandit leader Li Zaiyang was shot several times and fell to the ground. He struggled to throw himself into the river in an attempt to escape, but drowned. Bandit Mei committed suicide with a gun, while the two bandits Qian and Gao were captured alive, and four short guns were seized. At the same time, it was discovered that Yao Guilian, the Bao chief of Xinnan Township, was suspected of harboring bandits, and that Bao Yunsheng, a villager, had committed the crime of providing information to bandits. Both were arrested and sent to the Suzhou Headquarters for interrogation according to law. The reporter also learned that bandit leader Li Zaiyang was only in his twenties. He had once sided with the enemy during the puppet era and served as a secret agent. After the victory, he hid in Shanghai. It is rumored that the robbery case at the Jardine Matheson foreign firm on the Shanghai Bund was related to Li. The Shanghai Police Department searched for him but failed to find him and issued an arrest warrant.

Ship Robbery Case in Xieqiao, Haining

[Report from our Haining office] Xieqiao Town in this county is located along the Shanghai-Hangzhou line and has a prosperous market. On the afternoon of the 19th, Cai, the owner of the Xintong Cloth Store in the town, hired a boat to go to Haining. Near the Ruyi Bridge, four masked bandits with local accents suddenly ordered the boat to stop. Another person shone a flashlight from the bridge. When the boat approached the shore, they boarded the boat and searched for valuables. It is estimated that several hundred thousand yuan in cash and several valuable items were robbed. After the robbery, the bandits fled west. The police received the report and, since there had been robberies in the area from time to time, had taken precautions.

Gambling on Flower Associations Resurges in Various Counties of Taizhou

[Report from our Taizhou office] Gambling on flower associations has been prevalent in the counties of Taizhou. Previously, the District Commissioner's Office strictly prohibited it and ordered the county governments and townships to ban it, and the trend gradually subsided. Unexpectedly, recently gamblers in various counties have once again set up flower associations, set up listening tubes everywhere, and lured foolish men and women to bet in order to make a profit. They have been discovered in the villages of Huangyan, Wenling, Linhai, and Xianju. It is hoped that the authorities will strictly prohibit it.

Re-investigation Committee Again Visits Suzhou: Thoroughly Investigating Corruption in the Reception of Motor Vehicle Barracks

[Our Suzhou Dispatch on the 22nd] Wu Cangzhou, a member of the National Participation Council and the Jiangsu-Zhejiang-Anhui District Reception Investigation Group's Jing-Su Team, has recently arrived in Suzhou again from the capital. He is staying at the Lexiang Hotel. Our Suzhou-based special correspondent visited him on the afternoon of the 22nd to inquire about the mission of this trip. He informed us that after returning to the capital from Suzhou, he received a secret report alleging that the Second Battalion of the Twenty-Fourth Motor Vehicle Regiment stationed in Suzhou had concealed the reporting of enemy and puppet vehicles handed over during the reception process. It was alleged that they had secretly sold a portion, lent out a portion, and used another portion for business purposes. Furthermore, they were accused of reporting less gasoline received than they actually obtained, constituting flagrant and confirmed acts of corruption and dereliction of duty. Therefore, Team Leader Fan instructed him to come to Suzhou for a thorough investigation. He has already summoned the battalion commander, Jiang Xiaoyi, for questioning, but the commander has thus far avoided meeting him. He will conduct the investigation independently. Once evidence is collected, he will return to the capital to report and handle the matter according to the law. When the reporter inquired about the details of this corruption and the exact amounts involved, Mr. Wu stated that because the investigation was still ongoing, it was difficult to disclose information at this time.

[Our Xuzhou Dispatch] Zhao Xuefeng, a member of the National Participation Council and the Third Team of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang-Anhui District Reception of Enemy and Puppet Assets Investigation Group, stated that the investigation work is now nearing completion. However, many of the secretly reported cases involve too many parties, causing delays. Although the initial stages of each case are becoming clear, they have not yet been thoroughly investigated. In particular, in Bengbu, Anqing, Wuhu, Hefei, and other places in Anhui, there are still many major cases that have not been fully uncovered. It is necessary to enhance work efficiency to complete the mission as soon as possible. Therefore, it is planned to proceed separately, with Ma Jingchang responsible for the central Anhui region, Mr. Zhao responsible for the southern Anhui region, and Yang Wenbing responsible for the northern Jiangsu region. Mr. Ma has already departed for central Anhui, and Mr. Zhao is also about to depart for Wuhu.

Yixing Suffers from Rainwater Disaster: County Government Sends Personnel to Investigate

[Our Yixing Dispatch] Since the beginning of autumn, this county has suffered from excessive rainfall, causing flooding in low-lying areas of various districts. The rice fields have been submerged, significantly impacting the harvest. The heads of various townships have reported the disasters. To understand the actual situation, the county government has dispatched several land administration technicians to various districts and townships to investigate the extent of the damage.

Building a New Jiangxi: Designated Demonstration Counties

[Our Wuyuan Dispatch] Since the Head of State visited Nanchang last month and gave instructions to "Build a New Jiangxi," in addition to Nanchang being designated as a model city with a foreign urban construction expert specially assigned by the central government to assist in city construction, it has been heard that the provincial government is actively taking steps to implement the Head of State's instructions. They are first establishing demonstration counties and townships. Thirteen Education and Welfare Stations: Blessing Poor Children in Hangzhou

[Hangzhou Dispatch] The Zhejiang-Fujian Branch of the Executive Yuan Relief and Rehabilitation Administration (CRRRA), in cooperation with various charitable organizations, the Red Cross Society, and religious groups in Hangzhou, has established thirteen children's education and welfare stations. These stations accommodate a total of 1,800 poor and orphaned children. In addition to providing free meals daily, they also teach basic knowledge, including hygiene, music, handicrafts, and games. According to Director Xu of the Huilan Education and Welfare Station, because these children are usually malnourished, most suffer from ringworm, and many also have trachoma. The clinic established by CRRRA within the YMCA is providing free daily treatment. The Huilan Children's Education and Welfare Station is one of the thirteen stations. The station's premises are borrowed from Huilan Middle School, and CRRRA is responsible for providing the necessary food, such as rice, vegetables, milk powder, and canned goods. Books, furniture, and fuel are purchased with donations from the China Red Cross Children's Welfare Committee.

Regulations

(1) This column is absolutely open, and contributors are responsible for their writing. However, avoid lengthy submissions. (2) Do not attack individuals, and do not submit the same manuscript to multiple publications. (3) Contributors must indicate that their submission is for the "Reader Opinions" column and must provide their real name and address, but a pen name may be used for publication. (4) No payment will be provided for manuscripts in this column. (5) The newspaper reserves the right to edit submissions. (6) We will not reply to inquiries about whether a submission will be published. (7) The newspaper may forward submissions to relevant authorities for reference if necessary.

Hope for Extension of Route 7 Buses

The Route 7 public bus service began operating on Double Tenth Day (October 10th). It has indeed provided a great deal of convenience for residents of Hongkou. However, because there is no connection to trams or buses at the starting point at the intersection of Wusong Road and Broadway Mansion, we still feel that it is somewhat inadequate. Most of us Hongkou residents hope that the Route 7 bus service can be extended westward from Broadway Mansion along Suzhou Creek to the Sichuan Road Bridge. This would allow passengers to transfer to Route 17 trolleybuses and Route 2 public buses to reach the central district. The transportation authorities would not incur significant losses, and perhaps ridership and revenue would increase due to the connection to other services. The convenience for us would be substantial. We hope the authorities will reconsider and grant this request. (Cheng Quanlu)

Water Fruit Vendors Also Need to Make a Living

I am a civil servant. The other day, I was passing through the intersection of Fourth Ma Road and Jiangxi Road when I saw a vendor selling apples and pears. Suddenly, a vehicle for catching vendors arrived and took away about seventy percent of the vendor's fruit. The vendor wept and wailed, lying on the sidewalk, wanting to die! Many people felt sorry for him! I think that those who run small businesses are also seeking profit to support themselves. Currently, factories are shutting down everywhere, and there are many unemployed people. Even if they reopen, introductions are required. If even small vendors seeking profit cannot do business, what are they supposed to do? They also have wives, children, and elderly parents at home. Are they supposed to watch them starve to death? Therefore, I hope that the enlightened authorities can allow those who run clean small businesses to endure these difficult times, so they do not lose their livelihoods! (Chen Wenliang)

Reply via Post

Reply to Mr. Fugong Ping: (1) If a private middle school was approved for establishment by the puppet education administrative authorities, its graduates should be regarded as graduates of schools established by the enemy and puppets and subject to screening. (2) If the school was not approved for establishment by the puppet education administrative authorities, it cannot be regarded as a school established by the enemy and puppets. However, if the school has not been submitted to the education administrative authorities for approval, its graduates should still be subject to screening. (3) If the school is located in Wu County, its graduates should submit their applications directly to the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education for screening. (4) Graduates of the school who were admitted to national universities before 1946 should also be subject to screening.

Reply to Mr. Lu Liangcai: Regarding your previous letter appealing for improvements in the electricity supply, we have received a reply from the Pudong Electric Power Company stating: "Since the recent War of Resistance, our company's power generation equipment has been completely dismantled. Currently, the electricity supply is purchased and resold from the Shanghai Electric Power Company, which has severely restricted the supply due to insufficient capacity. As a result, the power shortage is becoming increasingly serious. Between 5:30 PM and 9:30 PM every evening, the demand for both lighting and power increases significantly. Although our company has published notices to all electricity customers to suspend usage during this time in order to reduce consumption, customers have not strictly complied, leading to a surge in load and frequent malfunctions. The brightness of the lights is uneven, and our company's prevention efforts are inadequate. We deeply regret this. We have now assigned employees to conduct inspections every evening. This situation may be alleviated in the future." We are providing this reply to you.

Supreme National Defense Council Approves Governance Guidelines for Pacification Zones

[Central News Agency, Nanjing, 21st] The Supreme National Defense Council, at its temporary meeting on the 16th, approved the Governance Guidelines for Pacification Zones and the following four measures: (1) Emergency Fiscal and Financial Measures, (2) Emergency Relief for Refugees, (3) Management of Land Tax and Grain, and (4) Land Management. The Governance Guidelines are as follows:

The purpose of governance in the pacification zones is to stabilize social order, alleviate the suffering of the people, strengthen grassroots politics, vigorously promote post-war reconstruction, develop civil rights, and foster the people's livelihood, in order to accelerate the thorough implementation of the Three Principles of the People. The guidelines are as follows:

(1) Conduct a census, reorganize the Baojia system (local administrative units), and strengthen self-defense organizations to ensure local security.

(2) Enforce the rule of law, strictly prohibit people from taking revenge on their own, and restore people's freedom of speech and assembly.

(3) Promote local autonomy, strengthen people's organizations, and establish people's representative bodies at all levels below the county level within three months.

(4) Carefully select grassroots administrative cadres and appoint local, fair, and capable individuals to serve as heads of townships, villages, and Baojia units.

(5) Punish corruption severely, vigorously implement performance evaluations, and establish a culture of clean and capable governance.

(6) In the pacification zones, farmers who own and cultivate their own land have the right to reclaim their land by presenting their ownership certificates. Farmers who do not cultivate their own land can retain their ownership by presenting their ownership certificates until the government handles the matter according to law. However, their land should continue to be cultivated by the current tenant farmers.

(7) In the pacification zones, the rent paid by tenant farmers to landlords shall not exceed one-third of the normal yield of agricultural products. If the rent is agreed to be paid in currency, it shall not exceed the equivalent value of one-third of the normal yield of agricultural products. Unpaid rent owed by tenant farmers before the recovery shall not be collected.

(8) In the pacification zones, if farmland has been illegally distributed, if the landlord is missing, or if it is impossible to restore the original situation, the county government should confiscate the land. The land price should be assessed according to law, converted into agricultural products, and land bonds issued by the Farmers Bank of China should be given to the legal owners, to be repaid in installments over the years. The aforementioned land bonds shall be based on agricultural products, and the repayment period shall not exceed fifteen years.

(9) The farmland confiscated by the government shall be given priority for cultivation in the following order, with the farmers cultivating it themselves, paying the price in installments, and obtaining ownership: A. The original tenant farmers before the disturbances; B. The current cultivators; C. Retired soldiers with the ability to cultivate the land and the families of soldiers who fought in the War of Resistance. The government should assist farmers who cultivate the land themselves and guide them in organizing cooperative farms.

(10) In the pacification zones, national taxes and land taxes in areas severely affected by disasters may be exempted for one year with approval. All outstanding taxes and levies from previous years before the recovery shall be waived. Illegal and excessive taxes and levies collected before the recovery shall be abolished.

(11) All currencies illegally issued in the pacification zones shall be invalidated and prohibited from use. The Central Bank shall fully supply legal tender (fapi). The Farmers Bank of China shall provide small, interest-free loans, and relief agencies shall provide emergency relief in legal tender or in kind to the impoverished people to maintain their livelihoods.

(12) Cooperative enterprises should be universally promoted in the pacification zones, and rural economies should be developed. The Cooperative Bank and the Farmers Bank of China should provide funding and provide agricultural loans. National and local financial institutions should establish branches to assist in the recovery of industry and commerce.

(13) The food for civilians and the military in the pacification zones should be统籌（unified planning) and supplied by the land and grain authorities. The authorities should register existing grain stores. After fully reserving what each household needs based on its population, the remaining grain can be purchased at the current local price. Illegally requisitioned grain should be confiscated and made public property.

(14) Grain shops, commercial establishments, and factories in the pacification zones should be registered and managed. Those who hoard goods for speculation and manipulate grain prices should be punished according to law. Military and government personnel who manage or requisition grain and engage in extortion or embezzlement should be severely punished.

(15) Special attention should be paid to the restoration and development of cultural and educational undertakings in the pacification zones. Students and teachers who have lost their education or employment due to the war should be recruited by educational institutions at all levels to enable them to resume their studies and work.

(16) National schools at all levels should be universally established in the pacification zones, and teachers should be carefully selected to accomplish their tasks and assist township and village heads in implementing government orders.

(17) Medical and health services and other necessary social welfare undertakings should be established in the pacification zones.

Fifty-One Nations' Representatives Gather in New York: UN General Assembly Opens Today; President Truman Will Attend and Deliver a Speech

[Our Dispatch] San Francisco, 22nd (Radio): The United Nations General Assembly will open in New York tomorrow. Representatives from all fifty-one nations have now arrived. Molotov held talks with Soviet representatives today, while Austin (the new permanent US representative to the UN General Assembly) held talks with US representatives. It is expected that the United States and the Soviet Union will engage in intense verbal battles at the General Assembly. According to Austin, the US delegation will be led by US Senator Connally, who will speak in the General Assembly's Political and Security Committee.

[Central News Agency, Washington, 22nd (Special Dispatch)] President Truman is scheduled to fly to New York tomorrow with his wife and secretarial staff. He plans to deliver the opening speech to the United Nations General Assembly, hold a tea party to entertain the representatives, and then return to Washington by train in the evening.

[Our Dispatch] San Francisco, 22nd (Radio): On the eve of the opening of the United Nations General Assembly, the US State Department engaged in various diplomatic activities with the foreign ministers and senior diplomatic representatives of various countries attending the General Assembly. The US clearly stated that it would urge the major powers to fulfill the Potsdam agreements and the decisions of the Moscow Four Foreign Ministers Conference, and to ensure that the Bulgarian elections to be held next Sunday and the subsequent elections in Poland and Romania are conducted in a democratic and free manner.

[Our Dispatch] San Francisco, 22nd (Radio): US Secretary of War Patterson issued a statement in the Scripps-Howard newspapers on the eve of the opening of the United Nations General Assembly, in which he strongly argued that if the world is to maintain peace, the United States must maintain a strong navy, army, and air force. Patterson denied that the invention of the atomic bomb has rendered the navy and army obsolete. He also stated that being well-prepared beforehand is better than risking another Pearl Harbor incident. Military weakness is a shortcut to war.

Regarding Togoland and Two Other Territories: Britain Proposes Trusteeship Conditions; Will Be Discussed by the UN General Assembly

[Reuters, London, 21st] The British Colonial Office issued a white paper today stating that the British government has submitted the terms of trusteeship for Tanganyika, Togoland, and Cameroon to the Secretary-General of the United Nations, requesting approval from the United Nations General Assembly. Britain plans to place these three territories under the trusteeship of the United Nations, while Britain retains the power to govern them. Britain will fulfill the basic objectives of the international trusteeship system stipulated in the United Nations Charter and will fully cooperate with the United Nations General Assembly and the Trusteeship Council to carry out the tasks stipulated in the Charter, facilitating periodic inspections of the three territories by personnel from the United Nations General Assembly and the Trusteeship Council. Britain will be responsible for peace, order, good governance, and defense within these three territories in order to safeguard international peace and security. For this reason, Britain shall have full legislative, administrative, and judicial powers in these three territories and may establish naval, land, and air force bases, build fortresses, station and use British troops, and take all measures deemed necessary by Britain. In formulating laws regarding the ownership and transfer of land and natural resources, the governing country shall take into account the laws of the local area and the existing and future interests of the residents. Land and natural resources shall not be transferred without the consent of the parties concerned. Britain shall also take the necessary steps to ensure equal treatment for the United Nations and its nationals in social, economic, and commercial affairs. Britain shall guarantee the freedom of nationals of all United Nations member states to enter, reside in, travel through, and acquire property in these territories. No discrimination shall be made against any national of the United Nations in the granting of rights to develop natural resources. Britain shall have the freedom to establish public services under reasonable conditions and may establish monopolies for the purpose of enriching administrative expenses. Britain shall guarantee the freedom of belief, thought, expression, publication, and assembly for the residents of these territories. Britain will also submit an annual report on governance to the United Nations General Assembly.

General Assembly News: Broadcasting to Begin Today; In Five Languages: Chinese, English, French, Russian, and Spanish

[Central News Agency, New York, 21st] The United Nations Department of Public Information officially announced that the first broadcast in the name of the United Nations and by United Nations personnel will begin on October 23rd, the opening day of the General Assembly. Commentary on all conference situations will be broadcast in English and French at any time. Broadcasting in the other three official languages, namely Chinese, Russian, and Spanish, will also begin simultaneously. The Chinese program will be broadcast from 2:45 AM to 3:45 AM US Eastern Standard Time (3:45 PM to 4:45 PM Nanjing time). The United Nations broadcasts to the Far East will be broadcast by radio stations such as KNBA 9490 kHz or 31.61 meters; KNAI 9494 kHz or 31.61 meters; OHKR 9650 kHz, or 31.9 meters. All United Nations broadcasts will include conference reports, behind-the-scenes news, and interviews.

UN Opium Committee: Restrictions on the Sale and Transport of Narcotics

[Agence France-Presse, London, 22nd] Mr. Mei, a representative of the United Nations Opium Committee, stated today that the worldwide anti-narcotics effort is currently being carried out by three organizations: (1) the Narcotics Advisory Committee, (2) the Central Opium Board, and (3) the Opium Committee. The latter two organizations will have to be merged in the future. Currently, the work is to determine the amount of opium that each country should receive based on statistics and medical needs. If the quantity exceeds the need, the Central Board has the right to request the exporting country to stop transporting to a specific country. Before the war, Japan evaded international control because the Japanese, encouraged by the government, secretly manufactured heroin and used this drug to transport it to China to erode the morale of the Chinese people. Germany also has a kind of artificial drug, similar to morphine, which is not made from poppy seeds and is difficult to control. The future of international drug prohibition is promising.

[Agence France-Presse, Lake Success, New York, 20th] UN Secretary-General Lai Yi recently sent a letter to General Assembly President, Belgian Foreign Minister Spaak, reporting on the work of the Security Council. The letter stated that the Iranian issue, the Spanish issue, and the issue of special measures stipulated in Article 43 of the United Nations Charter (namely, the issue of military units necessary for maintaining international peace and security) are still on the Security Council's agenda. The Greek issue, the Vietnamese issue, and the Syrian-Lebanese issue have been withdrawn.

Soviet Union Flatly Rejects

British Naval Commander-in-Chief Speech: Emphasizing the Defense of Maritime Communications; Reforming Weapons to Adapt to Modern Warfare

[Reuters, London, 22nd] British Naval Commander-in-Chief Admiral Cunningham stated today at the Trafalgar Day Commemoration that future wars will show that the weapons used by warships must undergo active reform. The industrial revolution has made Britain a large manufacturer of goods in peacetime and a large arsenal in wartime. However, continuous industrial production still depends on the continuous import of raw materials. If the source of raw materials and food is cut off in a relatively short period of time, the people of the British Isles will inevitably starve, and industry will inevitably come to a standstill. Therefore, maintaining our maritime communications lines is necessary. If the communications lines are destroyed, the enemy can defeat Britain without using atomic bombs or other new weapons.

Foreign Secretary Bevin Attends the House of Commons: Explains British Foreign Policy; Agrees that the Saar Region's Economy Should Be Linked to France; Hopes to Establish Lasting Peace with Japan

[Our Dispatch] Paris, 22nd (Radio, London): The British House of Commons began debating foreign affairs issues today. Foreign Secretary Bevin will attend and deliver a speech, the content of which will include the following four points: (1) British-Soviet relations, (2) the German question, (3) the Dardanelles Strait issue, and (4) British-Egyptian treaty negotiations. In addition, the Palestinian issue will also be involved.

Another dispatch: Foreign Secretary Bevin recently debated foreign policy in the House of Commons, stating that in order to avoid new disasters, the world should seek new solutions on a broad basis. He said, "If the United States had also participated in leading the handling of European issues after the First World War, the Second World War could have been avoided." Bevin綱 announced that he had informed the French government that he agreed to re-link the Saar region economically to France. The French franc can be officially circulated in Saar to replace the German mark, and France may establish a customs union with Saar. The customs agency should be managed by the Saar side, but the French side believes that it should be managed solely by France and should not be subject to the Control Commission in Berlin. The exact terms agreed to by the British side and whether they contain reservations are not yet known.

Bevin concluded: "The work of disarming Japan has been completed, and we sincerely hope to establish a lasting peace with Japan." In addition, the British troops stationed in Indonesia will be officially withdrawn by November 30.

Dardanelles Sovereignty Issue

Bevin then mentioned the Soviet Union's request to Turkey to jointly manage the Dardanelles Strait, saying that this request is essentially a violation of Turkey's territorial sovereignty.

Sidky is suffering from a cold and, on doctor's orders, did not leave his residence.

[United Press, London, 21st] Egyptian Prime Minister Sidky came here to revise the Anglo-Egyptian treaty. Today, he stated that so far, his talks with Foreign Secretary Bevin have progressed smoothly. However, government officials say that the negotiations are not close to resolving outstanding issues. It is reported that Sidky reiterated two final stances to Bevin: that British troops must withdraw from Egypt within two years, and that Sudan must be restored to Egyptian rule. Bevin insisted that British troops could not withdraw within three years and that the status of Sudan should be determined by the Sudanese people themselves. Therefore, Britain cannot agree to abandon the current Anglo-Egyptian condominium. The Sudan issue has consistently been the biggest obstacle in Anglo-Egyptian negotiations. The Egyptian side expects Sidky to return to Cairo on the 28th, and his next step may be to submit the Egyptian issue to the United Nations for discussion.

U.S. Airline Pilots Launch Full-Scale Strike

[United Press, Washington, 21st] The Airline Pilots Association, affiliated with the American Federation of Labor, called on its members today to strike on all of World Airlines' 28,270 miles of air routes due to failed demands for wage increases. Members of the association fly four-engine "Constellation" and "Sky Master" aircraft, traveling to and from the Atlantic, the Mediterranean, and the coastal valleys of the United States. This large-scale strike is a historical first in aviation. According to World Airlines, the union is now demanding that pilots of four-engine aircraft fly 20 hours per week and receive an annual salary of $15,000.

"Tokyo Rose" Innocent

Federal Bureau of Investigation Declines to Prosecute

[United Press, Los Angeles, 21st] Iva Toguri D'Aquino, an American-born Japanese woman, born in Los Angeles and educated at the University of California, returned to Japan in 1941 to visit relatives. The Pacific War broke out, and she stayed in Japan. During the war, she broadcast under the alias "Tokyo Rose," engaging in propaganda detrimental to the United Nations in the South Pacific. She was arrested in Japan after the war. After more than a year of interrogation by the Federal Bureau of Investigation, it has now been announced that she will not be prosecuted because "Tokyo Rose" is an abstract name, including at least twelve voices, and cannot be held responsible by one person.
