Overview of Important Issues at the United Nations General Assembly

[United States Information Service, New York, 21st] The 53 items on the agenda of the United Nations General Assembly are mostly issues of striving for a peaceful world and of lasting interest. After the United Nations General Assembly held in London last winter, representatives of 51 countries will face various important issues, such as the establishment of the United Nations Trusteeship Council, the Security Council's veto power, and the issues of various member states. United Nations Secretary-General Trygve Lie broadcast on a special United Nations program yesterday, emphasizing the importance of the General Assembly's actions, saying that the General Assembly is "an integral part of the United Nations organization's decision-making" and urging all parties to pay attention, saying that the General Assembly can consider all issues within the scope of the United Nations Charter in addition to the issues already considered by the Security Council. The timetable for considering the various issues stipulates that the General Assembly will hold plenary sessions for four days, after which the various committees should begin their work, and then hold plenary sessions again to discuss the progress of the various committees. The opening ceremony on Wednesday and the subsequent plenary sessions will be held at Meadows Park near New York; committee meetings will be held at the United Nations temporary headquarters at Lake Success. The General Assembly is expected to close in six and a half weeks (or December 7). During this period, the General Assembly will hold

450 sessions, of which approximately 30 to 35 will be plenary sessions, 90 will be major committee meetings, and the remaining sessions will be meetings of other subcommittees. It is expected that 70% of the General Assembly's work will be completed at Lake Success. Plenary and committee meetings are scheduled to be held on weekday mornings and afternoons and on Saturday mornings. There will be no meetings on Sundays. The General Assembly has six main committees, also known as plenary committees, because each committee has

representatives from 51 countries.

Goods Tax Bureau Levies New Taxes on Seven Items Including Cement and Wheat Flour

According to Fang Dongtan, Director of the Shanghai Goods Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance: After the destruction by the enemy and puppets, this Bureau was established in Shanghai a year ago. Although all tax systems are said to have reverted to the old rules, the preparations and implementation are no different from creating them from scratch. After repeated reorganizations and improvements, it has gradually progressed and is now expected to be on the right track. In total, since the beginning of the year, the amount of tax revenue has been increasing linearly every month. Starting in October, we have been ordered to add seven new taxes on cement, wheat flour, tea, foil, superstitious paper, beverages, cosmetics, and fur. We will naturally take "enriching the treasury and caring for merchants" as our duty. Although the collection of various new taxes has not yet reached a month, the various experiences can be roughly described. For example, tea is currently being promoted for export, and all exported goods are temporarily exempted from taxation to show encouragement. For fur, whether imported from overseas or transported from domestic production to the mainland, taxes have been paid according to regulations. Although merchants in this city have requested a delay in the collection of taxes on goods produced and sold locally, the Ministry has not approved it, and the Chamber of Commerce is being urged to earnestly persuade them. The taxes should be collected according to the plan. The remaining items such as cement have also been levied according to their production and sales conditions, either by sending personnel to collect taxes at the factories or by strictly examining them during transit and export to prevent loopholes. The overall goal is to promote the benefits to the fullest extent and benefit the treasury. As for rectifying discipline and rewarding whistleblowers, in addition to publishing public announcements in newspapers, we also hope that people from all walks of life will supervise us, he said.

A tea party was held by women's groups in this city to welcome Chairman Fang and Committee Member Lu, among others. Chairman Fang gave a speech. (Photo by China News Agency)

Electricity is the Soul of Shanghai! The Foundation of Shanghai's Prosperity Lies in Industry, and Industrial Development Depends on Electricity.

The degree of industrialization in Shanghai can be clearly demonstrated by the electricity consumption figures. The total power generation of the city is 130,000 kilowatts, with household use accounting for only one-third and industrial use accounting for two-thirds. Among the industrial electricity consumption, textile mills consume 42,000 kilowatts, accounting for half of the total. According to Director Zhao Zenggang's estimation, before the war, the work efficiency of textile mills was relatively high, and the amount of electricity required to produce each bale of yarn was 200 to 250 degrees; now, the efficiency of textile mills has not fully recovered, and the production of each bale of yarn requires 300 degrees of electricity. In addition to textile mills, other industries consume one-third of the city's electricity. According to the statistics of the Public Utilities Bureau, the order of electricity consumption for other industries is: (1) weaving industry, (2) flour industry, (3) paper making industry, (4) refrigeration industry, (5) rubber industry, (6) machinery industry, (7) wool weaving industry, (8) tobacco industry, (9) silk mills, (10) oil manufacturing industry. The Public Utilities Bureau has a power supply review organization to review the necessity of each industry for people's livelihood and determine the priority of their power supply. At present, the need for cotton cloth production is the most urgent, so the amount of electricity used by the textile industry will have to be increased in the future.

Power Plants Overburdened

Electricity is the mother of industry. The main reason why Shanghai's industrial productivity cannot be brought to its highest level is the lack of electricity. Shanghai's power plants are now overburdened, which is a sign of illness. Director Zhao of the Public Utilities Bureau explained this situation in detail at a dinner party of the Post-War Factory Rehabilitation Association. He said: The service time of power plants in this city is the highest in the world; in terms of the service coefficient, it is above 80 percent. This means that the machines in the power plants are working for more than 80 hours out of every 100 hours! Another fact is "excessive burden." Because the total power generation is 130,000 kilowatts, while the electricity consumption in Shanghai is as high as 150,000 kilowatts at two times of the day and night. Therefore, it is necessary to restrict electricity consumption in the future.

Four Ways to Increase Production

As for the future electricity control policy, the Public Utilities Bureau has put forward two slogans: "Save waste and increase production." The plans to cancel neon lights, restrict advertising lights, and reduce household electricity consumption by 30% are all based on the principle of saving waste. As for increasing production, the Public Utilities Bureau also has several directions for its efforts. The first is through the United Nations Relief and Rehabilitation Administration (UNRRA). UNRRA has five 2,000-kilowatt generators, and the Bureau hopes that three of them can be used in Shanghai to solve the city's electricity shortage. UNRRA has agreed to leave two, and the Bureau is continuing its efforts. This effort can increase the power by 4,000 to 6,000 kilowatts per month. Secondly, the power generation of the Shanghai Electric Power Company will also increase significantly by next spring. During the enemy and puppet period, the Japanese tried to改造 the machines, but the result was that the parts were damaged, and the power generation was reduced instead. After the takeover, the company hired engineers from the United States to thoroughly repair and improve them. It was originally scheduled to be completed in October, but because the repair was thorough, it will not be possible to generate electricity until January next year. An important machine was sent to the United States for repair, and it happened to coincide with the major strike in the United States. It was originally scheduled to be completed by the end of the year, but it will have to be postponed until February next year before it can be shipped back for power generation. These were all unexpected by the authorities, but it is hoped that they will not be in vain, because starting in February next year, the city will have 37,000 kilowatts of electricity more. The third way is in the Pudong area, where there is a British silk factory with a 2,000-kilowatt power generation facility before the war. During the war, it was dismantled by the Japanese and transported to a certain place, and it is now being moved back. The factory itself only uses 800 kilowatts of electricity, so after the generator is transported back, there will still be surplus electricity to supply the industry in the Pudong area. Fourth, in the Zhabei area, the current power generation is 4,800 kilowatts, which can be increased to 7,000 kilowatts after the machine is repaired. Because of these four sources of supply, the Director of the Public Utilities Bureau confidently told the post-war factory rehabilitation companies that the city's electricity shortage will be greatly improved by next spring.

Warships Help Generate Electricity

One thing can illustrate the Public Utilities Bureau's painstaking efforts to solve the electricity shortage problem. They are making the greatest efforts and preparing for the worst situation. If the city's electricity shortage becomes unbearable, the Public Utilities Bureau hopes to borrow electricity from the American warships in the Huangpu River. Their flagship can probably generate more than 4,000 kilowatts, and after its own use, there will be a surplus of 2,000 kilowatts. Of course, this issue is not simple. An American warship supplying electricity to a Chinese city is not something that the commander here can decide. The decision-making power is in the US Navy Department. In terms of power generation, a large warship is capable of meeting the needs of a city. A naval officer who studied in the United States told me that the power generation of the USS Roosevelt aircraft carrier and the USS Missouri battleship are several times greater than Shanghai's electricity consumption.

Electricity Prices Under Consideration for Increase

From the words of the Director of the Public Utilities Bureau, it is confirmed that the rumors of an increase in electricity prices are true. He said: The past electricity price regulations were 50 yuan per degree for small households, 73 yuan per degree for large households, and 84 yuan per degree for industrial use. In fact, this is a losing business. The cost of coal was originally 30,000 yuan per ton, but now it is 80,000 yuan per ton. For textile mills, the Public Utilities Bureau has specifically set up a "coal-for-electricity" method, which is equivalent to 200 yuan per degree of electricity; the profit from this is used to subsidize the losses of supplying other industries. This is not a sustainable solution. In terms of the raw materials of power plants, coal and diesel are used together. Since the adjustment of the exchange rate, the price of oil has soared, and the cost of electricity has also increased accordingly. The oil used by the Shanghai Electric Power Company is directly shipped from the United States, and the cost is very high. The reason why they have not immediately raised prices is still the result of negotiations by the Public Utilities Bureau. In summary, an increase in electricity prices is necessary; but how much to increase it is reasonable is still under study. Objectively speaking, from the perspective of people's welfare, the lower the electricity price, the better; but in today's Shanghai, electricity is too cheap, and there is also a lot of waste in households.

Some industrialists are deeply concerned about the cost of coal. They believe that the reason why electricity prices in Hong Kong are so low today is because the local power plants use Annam Hongji coal. They advocate relaxing the scale of coal control and allowing Vietnamese coal to come to China, which will definitely reduce costs. Another argument is to tap into the city's potential electricity. For example, the large textile mills and flour mills now have their own power generation equipment, but because it is cheaper to use public electricity, their own generators are idle. From the perspective of the city as a whole, this is a considerable loss, especially in today's Shanghai, where one more degree of electricity equals one more point of production.

Optimistic About Shanghai's Future

Shanghai is a large industrial and commercial metropolis, and the foundation of Shanghai's prosperity is built on industry. Director Zhao gave an optimistic outlook on Shanghai's future. He said that in 25 years, Shanghai will be a world-class metropolis with 7 million people, not just China's "window." In addition to the existing industrial zone, there should be four new industrial zones——Zhabei, Nanshi, the city center, and Pudong. A modern port will be built in the area around Rihui Port and Wusongkou. This beautiful vision of a large industrial metropolis is based on the shape of the Yangtze River Delta; looking even further, it is pinned on the large-scale hydropower project of the Three Gorges! Shanghai is the nerve center of China, and "electricity" is the soul of Shanghai!

Li Gufan Discusses the Mission of the Shipping Line Investigation Committee: Regulations Stipulate That Assignments of Liners on Various Lines to Maintain Transportation Should Not Be Neglected

According to Li Gufan, Director of the Shanghai Maritime Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications and Chairman of the North and South Ocean Shipping Line Investigation Committee: Domestic scheduled liners urgently need to be regulated. Therefore, the establishment of the Shipping Line Investigation Committee is urgently needed at present. The main tasks of the Shipping Line Investigation Committee have three principles: (1) Regulate and assign liners on various lines to maintain normal transportation. (2) Scheduled liners should not be neglected. (3) Fuel for liners, such as coal, is proposed to be allocated by the government as a public utility. It is heard that the Shipping Line Investigation Committee will convene relevant parties in the near future to discuss the direction of promoting future tasks. If shipping lines do not participate in the assignment and navigation of the committee, the committee will still allow them to operate freely, but they will not enjoy the above-mentioned rights.

Thorough Investigation of Forcibly Occupied Houses, Inspector Tang Left Shanghai Yesterday to Return to Beijing for Work, Expected to Conclude by Month's End

General Tang Enbo, acting Commander-in-Chief of the Army and concurrently Garrison Commander of Beijing and Shanghai, arrived in Shanghai on the 20th upon instruction from the Chairman to thoroughly investigate the forcible occupation of houses by personnel of the Party, government, and military, and to provide guidance for the city's winter defense conference. It is now learned that Tang's mission has been completed and he has left Shanghai by train to return to Beijing. Tang expressed satisfaction with the results of the investigation and highly commended the hard work of the personnel involved. Before his departure, Tang stated: As of now, the Garrison Headquarters has received a total of 1,327 requests for the removal of military personnel occupying houses. However, according to the investigation, actual cases of military personnel formally occupying houses account for only a quarter of the total, and all have been vacated after enforcement. The nature and handling methods of these 1,327 cases are as follows: (1) 143 cases involved enemy property occupied by military personnel and civilians. Because these houses were enemy property, they have been referred to the Enemy and Puppet Property Management Bureau. (2) 145 cases involved civilian houses occupied by government agencies, Party organs, and military units. The relevant agencies and units have been instructed to handle the matter through legal procedures and report to the Municipal Government and the Ministry of National Defense for record. (3) 205 cases involved occupation by Party and government personnel and civilians. As these individuals did not have military status, the cases have been referred to the Civil Affairs Bureau of the Municipal Government. (4) 415 cases involved occupation by military personnel, and orders to vacate have been enforced. (5) 419 cases involved rental disputes, and the parties concerned have been instructed to apply to the court or the Housing Rental Management Committee for mediation. The above enforcement work has been ordered to be completed by the 25th of this month. As for the cases of occupied houses still under investigation by the Garrison Headquarters, there are still over 150 cases, of which over 130 cases can be enforced immediately. The entire task is expected to be completed by the end of the month. In addition, Tang gave detailed instructions on the city's public order and winter defense. It is said that he may return to Shanghai again within days after returning to Beijing this time.

The Old Case of He Yuxiang's Martyrdom Six Years Ago Is Brought Up Again: The Case of the Former White Russian Soldier of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps Shooting the Lone Army Is Concluded, Squad Leader Testifies to Witnessing the Shooting, Lawyer Argues That Murder Cannot Be Proven

[Our Reporter] The court reopened the case of the White Russian soldier shooting the Lone Army yesterday afternoon. The witnesses, Ivanoff (former Major Commander of the White Russian隊of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps) and Shi Hongmo, former squad leader of the Fourth 行Lone Army, were summoned. Judge Wu Ronglin, Prosecutor Fang Zheng, and Clerk Xie Yinsheng took their seats. First, the defendant, Mitchiakov, was questioned about how many posts there were next to the Lone Army camp in September of the 29th year of the Republic. Mitchiakov replied: There were only seven posts in peacetime, but because the situation was tense at the time, it was increased to thirteen posts. On the day of the incident, Rakhitaev, the guard at the seventh post, also fired a shot. He did not know who fired the shot that killed He Yuxiang.

White Russian Commander Presents Diary

The presiding judge then questioned the witness Ivanoff. According to his testimony, there were a total of 320 White Russian隊guards guarding the Lone Army camp. On September 18 of the 29th year of the Republic, he was not present, and he was not in charge of the White Russian隊at that time. He only learned from the report after the incident that Mitchiakov fired a shot at 12:45 PM, and 30 seconds later, Rakhitaev, the guard at the seventh post, also fired a shot in the same direction. Ivanoff also presented the "Daily Diary" of the White Russian隊at the time to the court for reference.

A Loud Bang, and He Fell to the Ground

The witness Shi Hongmo, squad leader of the Lone Army, gave a very detailed account of the case, stating: Four days before the incident, an unfortunate incident had occurred in which the White Russians used tear gas and water taps to attack the Lone Army. The Lone Army members were all unarmed, and five brothers were killed or injured. He could not remember the names of the individuals due to the passage of time. The day of the incident was "September 18." Early in the morning, people came to the Lone Army camp to express their sympathy, but they were unable to enter because the White Russian隊had blockaded the entrance. By around 11 AM, more and more people had gathered. He (Shi Hongmo referring to himself) was ordered by Commander Xie to go to the gate to investigate. He stood shoulder to shoulder with the victim He Yuxiang on a long bench, peeking outside the wall. The defendant, Mitchiakov, was at the first post and aimed his gun three times in succession. The first two times he did not fire, but the third time he aimed for about a minute. With a loud bang, He Yuxiang fell to the ground. The bullet penetrated He Yuxiang's head and then injured another soldier, Gao Guangyun, in the leg, because Gao was standing on a wooden rack for washing his face behind He Yuxiang, so He Yuxiang's death was actually caused by Mitchiakov's bullet. Although the seventh post also fired a shot, it did not injure anyone. Judge Wu asked Mitchiakov again based on the witness's statement. Mitchiakov denied aiming three times and claimed that it was impossible for one shot to injure two people. After the witness made his statement, the presiding judge announced the start of the debate. The prosecutor stood up first and stated: The fact that Mitchiakov shot and killed He Yuxiang has been proven by witnesses, and Mitchiakov has also admitted to firing the shot, so he should be charged with murder.

Lawyer Explains the Circumstances at the Time

Liu Jiangang, the defense lawyer for the defendant, stood up and first explained the circumstances at the time, stating: At that time, the Japanese army was wreaking havoc in the suburbs of Shanghai and repeatedly negotiated with the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Concession to take over the Lone Army. The Municipal Council sent the White Russian隊to guard the Lone Army camp, ostensibly to watch over them, but in reality, to protect them in secret. He asked Frankling, who was in charge of the Shanghai Municipal Council at the time, and was told: On September 14 of that year, because the Lone Army raised the national flag without permission, the British army ordered them to lower the flag within three hours. The Lone Army did not comply, and the White Russian隊was ordered to release tear gas and use water hoses to disperse the Lone Army and lower the national flag, which caused a serious incident and tension. On "September 18," crowds gathered around the Lone Army camp. Mitchiakov's first post was especially crowded. Mitchiakov could not help but be alarmed under the encirclement. Six years ago, Mitchiakov was not yet twenty years old and was actually a minor. He asked Ivanoff, "Since the situation was so tense at the time, why didn't you send more guards to protect them, but instead let a minor take on this important task?" Now, although the defendant admits to firing the shot, it cannot be proven that he committed murder. There are two points to note in this case: (1) The death of He Yuxiang was not thoroughly investigated at the time because Commander Xie of the Lone Army camp did not allow the White Russians to enter the camp. Also, Mitchiakov was not the only one who fired a shot. Six years later, it is even more impossible to prove whose bullet killed He Yuxiang. Since the basis for the crime has not been established, how can he be convicted? (2) The act itself: Mitchiakov was surrounded by the public on the outside, and the Lone Army was responding on the inside, so the situation was extremely serious. According to the Lone Army camp guard instructions, the guard can fire his weapon if he encounters coercion or is in danger of being disarmed. The defendant, a White Russian, did not receive a good education, and his understanding of the law was probably not very clear. This order was issued by the British army, and the White Russian隊's enlistment documents also stated that they would abide by the regulations of the British army. Therefore, should the defendant be held legally responsible for firing the shot? Please, your court, decide and request that the defendant be acquitted or given the lightest possible punishment. At this point, the presiding judge announced the end of the debate and set the verdict for 2 PM on the 28th. The defendant was returned to custody.

The Inside Story of Shanghai Pickpocket Gangs (3)

— Huang Jiamo

The Hat Is Stolen, Gone Like a Wild Goose in the Sky

"Catching turtles" means snatching hats, especially expensive Western-style felt hats. Shanghainese commonly refer to it as "throwing the top palace," which has almost become a well-known term, but those involved have stopped using it. Usually, the "hard pickpocket" brothers who are particularly skilled at snatching hats are always in groups of two or three, lingering at tram and bus stops. They first spot the hat worn by a passenger near the window. Once the vehicle starts moving, they snatch it from the window and run away. The loser is not able to get off the vehicle immediately, and the vehicle is often packed like sardines. By the time the loser gets off the vehicle, the thief is long gone. When rickshaws and pedicabs are speeding, the felt hats of the passengers on the vehicle are also good targets. The pickpocket gang only needs to lightly stretch out their arms to grab the hat. Then they run madly in the opposite direction and hand it over to an accomplice. Even if the police pursue them, they often fail to catch them. This kind of "pickpocket gang" also "catches turtles" on the train platforms of the two railway bureaus. In recent years, the security at the railway platforms has been stricter, and the traces of this kind of people have not been often found on the platform.

The activity groups of the "hard pickpocket gang" are all controlled by the "uncle gang." The time and location are determined in advance, and "foreigners" who are not part of the gang cannot intrude and "steal their business."

The time for them to take action is set in the early morning, noon, and dusk. Because in the early morning, citizens are crowded at the train stations, and at noon and evening, pedestrians are crowded on the roads, both of which are conducive to escaping after the theft. Their activity locations are chosen in places with many side streets, or where the alleys are branched, and one of the skilled members of the group carries out the snatching and runs immediately. At this time, the loser will inevitably shout and chase after them. Then the accomplices pretend to be unrelated passersby and stop the loser to falsely inquire, in order to delay the loser's time and prevent pursuers who see the injustice. According to this strategy, they adapt to the situation and let the accomplice who snatched the item escape from danger through the side streets. These accomplices are called "wind blockers."

Sneaky and with Many Tricks

"Literary errand" is the second type of "eating bad rice." Unlike the forceful robbery of the "hard pickpocket" gang, they are sneaky "rats and dogs thieves." Because some of their behavior is relatively civilized, it is called "literary errand." The categories of their activities and performance methods are as follows:

(1) "Flipping over the head" - This gang always uses thick ropes or wooden ladders to climb over other people's walls or roofs to enter the house and then steal.

(2) "Prying open the fan" - The theft involves prying open the door with a small iron crowbar.

(3) "Running early morning" - Most of the people's houses are opened early in the morning to pour out the toilet or to clean. The petty thieves use this time to sneak in and grab something quickly.

(4) "Running to the lamplight" - Also known as "crow's head." In the evening dusk, most residents leave the back door ajar, and the petty thieves use the opportunity to sneak in and be active.

(5) "Going to heaven's watch" - People dry clothes on the drying racks on the sun terrace or in the courtyard every day, and most of the time, no one is watching. The petty thieves use long bamboo poles to pick down the clothes, regardless of whether they are dry or wet, and sweep them all away.

(6) "Cutting the crack" - If a residence locks the door, it shows that no one is inside. If the petty thief knows in advance that the family is rich, they will take advantage of the lack of preparation to break the lock and enter the house to steal calmly.

(7) "Running to the kiln" - This gang of thieves does not set a specific time, and their activity method is also very free. They steal anything they can get and leave immediately. No matter when, they take advantage of the gap to enter. They must also have the ability to distinguish. They will not take things that are not valuable. For example, if they enter a large family's house, they will pay attention to antiques, calligraphy and paintings, clocks, screens, and tripods in the hall.

(8) "Opening Tao Yuan" - Digging a hole in the wall to steal things, also known as "opening the kiln mouth."

(9) "Going to the bolt" - That is, a window-prying thief.

(10) "Lowering the bolt" - That is, a door-prying thief.

(11) "Breaking into the kiln" - Using the excuse of asking for directions, sneak into people's houses to steal.

"Hardware King" Trial Concluded, Awaiting Verdict, Zhang Lianfang's "Great Reasoning" Brings Family to Tears

[Our Reporter] Zhang Shufang, known as the "Hardware King" of Shanghai, was arrested after the victory on suspicion of being a traitor. The High Procuratorate concluded the investigation and filed a public prosecution, listing three charges: (1) Serving as the Chairman of the Puppet Shanghai Hardware Industry Association, (2) Serving as the Director of the Puppet Hardware, Steel, and Copper Strip Joint Office, (3) Serving as the Bao長of the 6th Bao of the 2nd Lian保of the Puppet Huangpu District, with acts of requisitioning iron on behalf of the enemy. The High Court held several hearings to investigate the case, and the debate court was concluded yesterday afternoon. The verdict is scheduled to be announced on the 29th of this month.

Zhang testified in court yesterday: He had resigned from the chairmanship of the association more than 20 times, but it was all because of the "recommendation and retention" of his colleagues that he did not succeed. This was purely to seek "welfare" for his colleagues and did not harm the country. As for the Pacific War that started on December 8th, 1941, the Japanese took planned actions and sealed up all the warehouses of the four industries in this city: hardware, copper strips, copper and tin, and steel. They ordered that the inventory must be registered. Under the circumstances at the time, there was no way to resist, so a joint office was organized to cope with it. The office only had a secretary and a tea boy, and there were no titles such as members or directors. It was only a place where colleagues gathered daily to seek to rescue materials and protect industry and commerce, so as to preserve a little vitality for the country. After the establishment of the Hardware Office, it did not use hardware to aid the enemy, nor did it collect hardware on behalf of the enemy. Because the colleagues had already registered the inventory with the enemy, they would take as much as they wanted. As a result, the enemy navy took 1,200 tons, and the enemy army took 700 tons, totaling about 2,000 tons. This matter did not go through the joint office, but was a separate matter for each colleague. As for serving as a puppet 保長, it was because he had some status in Shanghai that he was forced to take on the role. In 1944, the enemy puppets launched a city-wide 保甲獻iron campaign. When the 保長大会was convened, he did not attend. As a result, the Lian保長ordered the 保長to转甲長to转 to each household and have each household send the iron directly to the puppet police局, without going through the 保長office. Under the circumstances at the time, the citizens were also forced to do so. He was purely a businessman and had no intention of aiding the enemy. In the early days of the war, he once fled to Hong Kong because 76 号forced him to participate in a puppet organization. Later, he returned to Shanghai at the insistence of his colleagues to maintain the association. Later, he secretly transported materials to the interior but was known to the enemy, so he was captured in the north and tortured. At that time, he only hoped that the days would be bright again. Now, he has been detained for more than a year on the charge of being a traitor, which is really an extreme injustice. If he was willing to betray the country, please punish him severely; otherwise, please consider the facts and acquit him. At this point, his family members who were in the audience could not help but weep. After the trial, the defendant was still escorted back to prison by the bailiff.

Shen Fenggang Constantly Quibbling

Shen Fenggang, a key figure in the puppet government's special agent force, who successively served as the Director of the Third Office of the Puppet Special Agent Headquarters, the Captain of the First Special Agent Brigade, and the Director of the Puppet Jiangsu Province Qing乡Inspection, was accused of killing many underground comrades. The High Court has held several hearings to investigate the case. Yesterday morning, he was questioned again. Shen still did not admit to any of the crimes listed in the indictment. The court set aside the case for further questioning.

Li Zuyu Receiving the Interrogation (Photo by China News Agency)

Shenzhou Telegraph Agency Resumes Business

Yesterday, a banquet was held with colleagues to exchange ideas.

Shenzhou Telegraph Agency is a purely private news and telegraph organization, established in 1936 by Mr. Mi Xingru, the former President of the 申时Telegraph Agency. Answers to Readers' Legal Inquiries

(1) Forged Lost Receipt

A reader named Yi-ming asks for clarification on several legal questions: In the 32nd year of the Republic of China [1943], Mr. Jia mortgaged two shares of land to my late father through Mr. Yi as an intermediary. After our hometown was occupied in the 29th year [1940], Mr. Yi took advantage of his power to buy the land from Mr. Jia. I was not notified at the time (Mr. Jia has now passed away). After the victory, I entrusted someone to negotiate with Mr. Yi, who colluded with my stepmother to forge a lost receipt, stating that when Mr. Jia previously mortgaged the land to my late father, the loan receipt was lost and the debt had been repaid. The lost receipt was signed with my late father's seal. I have several questions and would appreciate your answers: (1) The original intermediary and the buyer were both arranged by Mr. Yi, and I was not notified. Can I deny this transaction? (2) Mr. Jia has passed away. Can his property be considered mine and can I apply for land registration? (3) Can I sue for forging my late father's lost receipt? (4) Can publishing a notice to invalidate my late father's seal be used to invalidate the lost receipt at the same time?

[Answer from Lawyer Cao Ya-xia] (1) No. Because after the property owner sets a mortgage, they can transfer the property to others, and there is no regulation that the intermediary for the mortgage cannot also be the buyer. (2) No. It is not permitted by law for the ownership of the mortgaged property to be directly transferred to the mortgagee. (3) If it is indeed forged, you can sue for the crime of forging documents. (4) Publishing a notice of invalidation cannot invalidate a receipt that was previously established.

(2) Redemption of Mortgaged Land

Ren Cheng-fu asks: In the third year of the Republic of China [1914], my great-grandfather mortgaged a piece of land with a 'living deed' for sixty silver dollars, and built a house on it. The contract clearly stated a five-year term for redemption. After five years, thirty-five silver dollars were added, and another contract was written, stating that when redeeming, the original sum should be returned together, with no shortage. In the thirteenth year [1924], ten silver dollars were borrowed with a monthly interest rate of three percent. The house was burned down by the enemy during the war. When the enemy surrendered, I wanted to rebuild the house on the land, but the mortgagee intends to redeem it. I can barely afford to build the house, but I worry about future disputes. Legally speaking, can the land be redeemed by the mortgagee? Please answer in your column.

[Answer from Lawyer Cao Ya-xia] According to Judicial Yuan Interpretation No. 2558, item 7, "For pawn rights established before the implementation of the Regulations for Clearing Real Estate Pawns, if a term is specified, redemption is allowed within two years after thirty years from the date of the pawn, regardless of whether the term has been extended by contract." The Regulations for Clearing Real Estate Pawns were implemented in the fourth year of the Republic of China [1915]. This pawn was established in the third year of the Republic of China [1914], and can be handled according to the above interpretation. The legal period for redeeming pawned items can be extended by two years after the implementation of the Supplementary Regulations for Handling Civil Litigation After Recovery, as stated in Article 7 of the same regulations, if the legal period for redemption could not be observed due to the war. Therefore, legally speaking, this pawned item can still be redeemed.

Wool Yarn Price Evaluation: Subcommittee Investigates Cost Standards, Divided into Three Grades, Fine Wool Yarn to be Separately Determined; Future Deliveries Limited to Members of the Same Trade Association

[Our Report] The Wool Yarn Review Committee established by the Social Affairs Bureau held its second meeting yesterday afternoon at 10:00 AM. Representatives from the Wool Yarn Industry Association, the Commercial Association, Chen Qi'en, Shen Lai-zhou, and representatives from Bee Factory and EWO Factory, among others, attended. Representatives from the Municipal Council and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce were also present. Director Gu Bingyuan presided over the meeting. First, the Industry Association reported on cost calculations, and the Commercial Association reported on recent market conditions. It was noted that the market price of wool yarn had fallen by 20 to 30 percent in the last ten days. Based on the current market price of raw wool and factory taxes, prices seemed to be stabilizing. Everyone was pleased, but the task of reviewing standard prices required further effort. It was decided to establish a subcommittee to investigate actual costs, with representatives from the Bureau, the Industry Association, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, to serve as a basis for determining standard market prices for wool yarn. It is proposed to divide the evaluation into three grades: the first grade is made of 56 counts or more, such as Bee, Cat, Hero, Popular, and Earth brands; the second grade is made of less than 56 counts, such as Golden Dog and Beauty brands; and the third grade is made of less than 48 counts, such as Scholar and Girl brands. The cost investigation will target these grades, but these three grades are all four-strand coarse wool yarn. The ratio for fine wool yarn will be determined separately and will fluctuate accordingly. Regarding the sale of imported raw wool and yarn by trading companies, it should be limited to the wool yarn industry. Those operating wool yarn in the market should join the Industry Association. The Industry Association representatives strongly advocated for these points, which were approved in principle. It was also decided that future deliveries of wool yarn from factories must be limited to members of the Industry Association to prevent disruption by outsiders.

Cotton Export Exchange Can Be Converted to Loan

[Our Report from Nanjing on the 22nd] The method of exporting cotton from production areas to cotton-using areas for export exchange this year was previously approved in principle by the Joint Treasury with five prices. It is now reported that the Treasury has now issued three supplementary measures: (1) After September 20th, cotton purchased by factories from production areas can be converted into loans after arriving at the factory site, according to the original principles. The maximum period is 45 days. (2) Cotton already purchased and stored by factories may not be converted into loans. (3) When applying to convert the cotton export exchange into a loan, factories must provide the original export exchange documents or equivalent documents for verification in order to assist in production and sales and prevent hoarding. The above measures have been telegraphed by the Joint Treasury to all branches for compliance, and to all branches to inform local offices.

Amidst Controls, Yarn Factories Have Three Wishes: Allocation of Cotton, Uninterrupted Power, and No Rigid Price Limits

Mayor Wu, Chairman of the Textile Control Committee, decided the day before yesterday to allocate 10,529 bales of yarn first, with the price and date to be determined separately. According to yarn factory opinions, it is difficult to achieve fairness and rationality when materials are scarce. Although yarn factories appear prosperous on the surface, they are actually empty shells. For example, the current price limit is 1.55 million yuan per piece, but the cost of three piculs of cotton is about one million yuan, plus electricity, interest, and other expenses, which already exceeds the price limit. There was a time when they were slightly better than other industries, but the current situation is very difficult. For example, even if the electricity supply is not considered, the price of electricity is a problem. The original price of electricity was 84 yuan per unit, but since the exchange of coal for electricity, the price of each ton of coal is 120,000 yuan, which has invisibly increased the price of each unit of electricity to 200 yuan. In terms of productivity, in the past, each shift worked 12 hours a day, two shifts a day. Now each shift works 10 hours a day, 20 hours a day. In the past, there were ten days in a week, but now there are seven days in a week, and sometimes power outages must be rotated. Even if the factory wants to increase production, it is limited by various facts. The solutions that yarn factories currently hope to resolve are: first, implement the allocation of cotton, and the government should try its best to supply cotton raw materials to reduce costs; second, supply electricity. The current rotating power outages and sudden power cuts affect the increase in production; third, implement evaluation instead of rigid price limits.

Banks Should Pay Even if the Draft Stub Has Not Arrived

According to the usual practice of Chinese banks, if a remitter remits money from a bank in Location A to Location B, holding the demand draft issued by the bank in Location A and sends it to the payee. When the payee collects the money from the bank in Location B, the bank in Location B usually only allows payment after verifying that the draft and its stub or counter-stub are consistent. If it is a clean payment on delivery, the stub can be ignored. However, the Negotiable Instruments Law does not stipulate that payment should be made only after the stub is verified. It stipulates that the holder of the instrument should present it for payment on or within two days after the due date. If it is overdue by three days, the holder of the instrument can legally seek recourse from the bank. The legal provisions and customs are not entirely consistent. The Central Bank recently received a notice from the Joint Treasury forwarded from the Ministry of Finance, informing that banks should fulfill their payment obligations within the legal time frame in order to protect credit and facilitate customers. Moreover, the Negotiable Instruments Law stipulates that payment can be postponed for three days with the consent of the holder of the instrument, leaving room for maneuver. In addition to verifying the stub, there are other methods that can be used to identify the authenticity of the draft. Therefore, it will be much more convenient for payees to collect money from banks in the future.

Professor Ryan of the United States Delivers Lecture at Ministry of Education - Modern Educational Trends Emphasize Breaking Down Class Barriers, Flexible Curricula, and Addressing Interpersonal and Social Relationships in Teaching - United States Recently Establishes Association for Early Childhood Education

[Our Dispatch from Nanjing, 22nd] The Ministry of Education invited Professor Ryan from the United States to deliver a lecture at the Ministry's auditorium yesterday (the 21st) at 3:00 PM. Over 400 people attended, including Ministry of Education staff, middle school teachers from Nanjing, and normal school students. The lecture was titled "Modern Educational Trends." Professor Ryan's lecture was translated by Ms. Xiong Zhi, and recorded by Mr. Ye, a Ministry of Education staff member. The main points of the lecture can be summarized as follows: (1) All aspects of education must be considered. (2) Children should receive a complete education. Break down the class system, teach according to aptitude, and group students according to individual characteristics and talent development. Curricula should be flexible and adaptable, not only in elementary schools but also in middle schools. (3) Teach according to environmental conditions. Teaching from books alone, discussing flowers and birds in the desert, or rivers and seas in the mountains, is mere empty talk on paper and difficult to achieve practical results. (4) The true meaning of education emphasizes the whole life. In addition to knowledge, pay attention to the development of emotions. For example, a nurse should not only rely on medicine for treatment but also provide gentle care and comfort to the patient to speed up recovery. (5) To achieve the goals of the new education, it is not just about the teaching materials; teachers must have a new perspective, understand the various relationships between people and society, and make these relationships the object of teaching. Otherwise, they can only teach books and not educate people. Professor Ryan also stated that this new educational trend is not unique to the United States; all countries in the world share the same trend. Recently, educationalists from sixteen countries in the United States have joined together to establish the Association for Early Childhood Education, which has issued a declaration stating that the barriers between schools and society should be opened up to create closer links and communication. The declaration also calls for changing the school system's excessive reliance on grades and rote learning, viewing schools as places for training cooperation and equality, and ensuring the livelihood stability of those engaged in education and encouraging outstanding young people to serve in education and work hard.

Northeastern Youth Out of School, Gan Jiaxin, Appeals to Executive Yuan for Relief

National Student Statistics - Number of University Students Doubles Compared to Pre-War

[Nanjing, 22nd] According to statistics from the education authorities, the number of students nationwide this year is: (1) 120,000 in universities and colleges (excluding the Northeast and Taiwan); (2) 1,163,000 in secondary schools; and (3) 18,602,239 in primary schools, including kindergarten students. It is reported that this number has increased compared to pre-war levels. According to Ministry of Education statistics, there were only 43,000 university students nationwide in 1936. The number has now more than doubled. However, given the vast territory of our country, the problem of students out of school remains very serious, and the lack of qualified teachers and their low pay also urgently require a solution.

Middle and Primary Schools Not Allowed to Operate Concurrently

The Ministry of Education Has Already Stipulated Measures

Regarding the reorganization of concurrently operated schools in this city, the Ministry of Education has stipulated the following measures: (1) Private middle schools are not allowed to operate primary schools concurrently. Those that have already done so and have achieved good results should set up separate school buildings. (2) Public and private primary schools with branch schools should merge into the main campus. (3) Middle school departments operating concurrently based on primary schools will be ordered to cease operations.

Youlian Wins Women's Team Final Spot in Guo Zhen Cup Volleyball Tournament - Wuben Eliminated 3-1 in Yesterday's Semi-finals - Men's Tournament: Guangdong Loses to Soviet Union

[Our Dispatch] There were two semi-final matches in the Guo Zhen Cup Volleyball League last night. Both were evenly matched contests with a lot at stake, and the fighting was intense and exciting. In the women's division, Youlian defeated Wuben 3-1 to win a spot in the final. In the men's division, Guangdong lost to the Soviet Union 2-3.

Youlian Wins After Hard Fight

Since Wang Wuli transferred from Wuben to Youlian, the latter's strength has increased sharply and it seems to have a solid chance of winning the championship. However, Youlian's performance yesterday was obviously rusty, and there was a lack of coordination between the various positions. According to Chen Meizhen of Youlian, the team members have been neglecting practice due to their jobs and studies, which is not without reason. Wuben fought hard despite its disadvantage, so it posed a great threat to Youlian. Youlian won with great difficulty. Now that Youlian has defeated Wuben, it will meet Youdui in the final. Based on yesterday's battle, it will still have to make an effort.

In the women's division match between Youlian and Wuben, Lu Zhaoshan of Youlian served first, and Li Bo of Wuben missed, giving Youlian a point. The players of Wuben were cautious, and the scores remained close. At the end of the first set, Youlian took the lead with a score of 21-19. In the second set, Youlian once led 7-1, but Wuben chased and surpassed them 9-8. Youlian tried to recover, but Lu Cuifang's movements were slow, revealing a weakness that Wuben took advantage of. As a result, Wuben tied the score with a score of 21-14. The competition in the third set was even more intense, with the scores fluctuating and the tension palpable. After several ties, Youlian relied on Chen Meizhen's successful spikes to win the set 21-19 again. In the fourth set, Wuben once led 11-5, but Youlian chased to 14-11 and then took the lead. As a result, Youlian won 21-18 with a final effort, eliminating Wuben with an overall score of 3-1.

Guangdong Suffers Miserable Elimination

The Soviet Union was determined to win the championship. Having lost the league, it was even more ambitious for the Guo Zhen Cup. The same was true of Guangdong. Unfortunately, its star player Zheng Yiquan was unable to attend due to illness, which was a significant loss. Guangdong's defeat yesterday was entirely due to its weak spikes. The Soviet Union used both spikes and blocks, and had sufficient stamina. After the score became 2-2, Guangdong could not hold on.

In the men's semi-final, Guangdong and the Soviet Union took the court. Guangdong proceeded cautiously, and the scores were close. When the teams switched sides, Guangdong led 11-10. In the second half, the two sides engaged in close combat, and Guangdong won the first set 21-16. In the second set, the Soviet Union tried to rally and scored repeatedly, tying the score 21-12. The competition in the third set was even more intense. Guangdong trailed by 17 points, the situation was critical. It launched a counterattack, tying the score at 20. However, it lost the set again 21-23. In the fourth set, Guangdong suddenly found its rhythm, leading 11-6. As a result, Guangdong recovered its lost ground 21-16, tying the score at two games each. In the final set, both sides were cautious, and the game became even more tense. At 11-8, the Soviet Union became even more ferocious, and Guangdong suffered a crushing defeat of 13-21, and the Soviet Union defeated Guangdong 3-2 overall.

National Assembly Representatives' Registration Procedures - Preparatory Committee of National Assembly Cables Provincial and Municipal Governments to Inform

The travel expenses and transportation for representatives attending the National Assembly from all over the country have been determined by the Preparatory Committee of the National Assembly. It is heard that the relevant matters for representatives coming to Beijing have been telegraphed to the provincial and municipal governments to be conveyed to the representatives. The six items are described below:

(1) Register at the National Assembly Registration Office at No. 10 Zhongshan Road (i.e. Xinjiekou) in Nanjing on November 2, submit the certificate of election and the attendance notice issued by each election office, and submit four 2.5-inch portrait photos.

(2) The provincial and municipal governments are requested to advance the travel expenses for each representative according to the standards.

(3) The Assembly will provide meals and accommodation for each representative during the meeting period, but only for the representative himself.

(4) When each representative leaves for Beijing, please obtain a certificate from the provincial or municipal government or election office at the place of departure, stating the place of departure and whether the travel expenses have been advanced. Those who do not go through the provincial capital for centralization should have the certificate issued by the local government or competent authority. (Overseas representatives, please obtain certification from the local consulate. Military representatives, please obtain certification from the unit commander.) The certificate will serve as the basis for sending travel expenses.

(5) This Committee has entrusted social service agencies or provincial, municipal, and county governments in Chongqing, Guiyang, Lanzhou, Hankou, Changsha, Jiujiang, Bei____, Tianjin, Qingdao, Shanghai, Guangzhou, Shenyang, Dalian, Changchun, Xi'an, Kunming, Guilin, Xiamen, Taipei, Xuzhou, Hami, Dihua, Fuzhou, Zhenjiang, Kaifeng, Taiyuan, Gui Sui, Jinan, Zhijiang, Chengdu, Hangzhou, Hefei, Nanchang, Jialan, Xining, and other places to set up representative transportation reception stations to handle transportation and reception matters. Representatives are requested to contact the nearest station.

(6) Representatives who have already registered in the previous session do not need to register again, but please come to the Committee to complete the registration procedures before the start of registration this time, exchange the previous certificates and badges for new certificates and badges. Representatives who registered last time are still requested to complete the registration procedures.

Page 9

Thunderous Destruction Crushes Zhangjiakou, One Gourd Spared From Total Destruction: More of a Funeral Procession Than a Tour!

— Eighteenth Dispatch From Beiping, Our Reporter Song Shaobai

On the eighteenth, I, as a reporter, accompanied the "Chinese and Foreign Reporters' Tour Group to Zhangjiakou" from Beiping to Zhangjiakou. It was more of a "funeral procession" than a "tour." This official said solemnly during a speech at the Suiyuan Anniversary Week earlier this month: "Although we won the battle, there is only sorrow, not joy, because those who died were all Chinese!" Zhangjiakou experienced this disaster, and the destruction was entirely of the people of our country and their hard work.

At 8:30 in the morning, people boarded the plane. For the convenience of photographers, the plane circled over Beiping twice before flying northwest. Because it was uphill, it took a few more minutes to reach Zhangjiakou's airspace, where it circled for an hour. From the plane, Zhangjiakou, surrounded by mountains, looked like a gourd, an unsuitable place to defend. No matter Zhangbei to the north, Chaigoubu to the west, or Xuanhua to the east, once the attacking forces controlled them, the defending troops in this gourd would have to consider withdrawing as soon as possible. Zhangjiakou, this "gourd," seemed to have been spared from total destruction due to its terrain.

Zhangjiakou has two airfields. The larger one in Yulinbu has been completely destroyed by the communist army. From the plane, we could see the concrete runway riddled with bomb craters. We landed at the smaller Yaoguantun airfield. We boarded the trucks prepared by the Twelfth War Zone to enter the city and saw the aftermath of the disaster along the way.

Citizens Awaken From a Nightmare

As the trucks drove through the streets, we saw rows of people lining the sides, seemingly stretching endlessly. The reporters seemed excited, but those sitting on the ground did not stand up, nor did we hear cheers. Upon closer inspection, the triangular flags read, "Welcome to General Commander Chen, who has worked hard." The reporters understood. The people were all dazed and expressionless, showing neither joy nor sorrow, as if awakening from a nightmare, not yet fully clear. Most shops and houses had national flags hanging, but the colors and wrinkles did not look new. Later, when we asked a merchant, he said that they were not usually hung. Many people stood in front of the shops, seemingly watching the excitement without a clue. Aside from those clearing rubble and rows of stalls waiting for soldiers with legal tender, we saw few people working. Although small shops were open, they were desolate. Citizens did not have legal tender to buy things, and "border currency" had lost its value. (The slogans have been renewed.) On the bulletin boards, "Zhangjiakou Garrison Headquarters Notices" were posted. A crowd surrounded each notice. The plaques of "Liberation Hotel," "Xinhua Bookstore," "Jin-Cha-Ji..." hung high, but some had been burned. The Qingfeng Grand Theater announced "Drama performances begin today," and the brothels "×× Academy" and "×× Pavilion" were open as usual. Here, we could no longer see any traces of the "Mongolian Administration" period, replaced by our own destruction and slaughter.

The Station Is the Most Severely Damaged

The station was the most severely damaged. A long row of buildings was completely burned. Train cars were charred, and locomotives collided head-on. Undamaged machines were put together to form a locomotive, which is scheduled to be used today to connect Xuanhua and Zhangjiakou. The power plant was completely destroyed. Wires dragged on the streets, but a small generator had been repaired. Electricity was restored to the official's office on the seventeenth. Automatic telephone machines were completely burned. It is said that this is the most difficult to restore. Important components of the broadcasting station have been removed. A small radio station may be restored soon. The most fortunate thing is the water supply, which was saved by the factory workers, who secretly removed the fuse to the landmine.

With the stationing of troops, a "Temporary Political Affairs Committee of the Twelfth War Zone" has been established in Zhangjiakou to handle post-war affairs. The chairman of this committee is Zhou Jun, the deputy director of the political department of the Twelfth War Zone. The committee's urgent tasks include the following: land ownership issues, marriage issues, confessions and surrenders of communist party personnel, currency regulation, and emergency relief.

Restoring Land Ownership

Regarding land ownership, the commander has received instructions from the central government that, in principle, as long as the owner provides evidence (those who have lost evidence can have neighbors testify), their ownership can be restored regardless of the "struggle" they have undergone. However, in order to consider the losses of the cultivators, the cultivators' right to use and harvest is also recognized. Rent is not allowed to exceed 15% of the total harvest. If it has gone through more than two "struggles," the initial cultivator should get 35%, the intermediate cultivator should get 35%, the harvester should get 25%, and the landlord remains at 15%. This is a temporary measure until the end of the year, after which the "land limit policy" will be implemented according to the land law. The planned quota is about 20 mu per person, and no more than 200 mu for a family of five. The rent will be even less than the "25% rent reduction" method. Based on the actual situation, a standard similar to the current transitional method will be set, that is, the rent should not exceed 15% or 10%. According to Zhou Jun, chairman of the Temporary Political Affairs Committee, this method of limiting rent has already been implemented in western and eastern Suiyuan. It is 10% in western Suiyuan and 15% in eastern Suiyuan, accounting for about one-third of the province, and there has not been much difficulty. However, the difficulty in implementing the land limit method in the future is whether the central and local governments can raise enough money to buy the landlords' land and distribute it to the landless. According to his estimate, the local government can raise 10% or 20%. Therefore, it cannot be determined whether this policy can be effectively implemented next year. But according to Zhou, in order to practice the Principle of People's Livelihood and counter the Communist Party's set, this is necessary and urgent.

Currency Issues Are Troublesome

Currency issues are also a relatively troublesome issue at present. The "Border Region Currency" issued by the Communist Party has been banned. All that is available now is the 40 million legal tender that the Twelfth War Zone brought with them. The shortage of small denominations also needs to be resolved immediately. Therefore, the commander's office loaned the Chamber of Commerce 20 million and allowed them to issue temporary small-denomination circulating notes, which began to be used on the eighteenth. Zhangjiakou's prices have not yet been stimulated. Flour is 400 yuan per catty, rice is 500 yuan, and white cloth is 90,000 yuan per bolt. But people fear that the price increase after the resumption of traffic and when there is no shortage of currency will be alarming, because Zhangjiakou actually has very little left. Someone from the Central Bank arrived in Zhangjiakou on the same plane as the reporters to prepare for the establishment of a branch. Marriage issues are easier to resolve. The principle has been set that those without problems are free to choose, and those with problems are based on the woman's opinion.

Registering Workers

The number of unemployed workers in Zhangjiakou has not yet been counted. Including the workers of the Longyan Coal Mine in Xuanhua, there are no less than tens of thousands. There are many others who urgently need relief due to the war. For workers, the Temporary Political Affairs Committee decided to register them immediately, allow them to repair the damaged factories, and pay them 1,000 to 1,500 yuan per day, equivalent to relief in exchange for work. In addition, the Executive Yuan Relief Committee also had five people arrive on the same plane as the reporters, bringing 40 million in cash to handle emergency relief.

The Self-Confession Movement Is Very Effective. More than 2,500 people have confessed. The authorities announced that as long as they confess and obtain a guarantee from the Baojia, they will be given a chance to start anew and will not be held accountable for the past. At the same time, retaliatory actions are prohibited. It has been a week since Zhangjiakou was recovered, and no retaliatory actions have been seen. The general public seems to be very enlightened, which the authorities think is very good.

Textbooks Cause Panic

Zhangjiakou originally had more than 40 elementary schools, with tens of thousands of students. After this change, they have not suffered too much damage and have all resumed classes. The Chinese Communist Party textbooks have been abolished, but new textbooks have not yet been settled, which is an urgent problem to be solved. Schools above the secondary level previously included municipal middle schools for boys and girls, agricultural vocational schools, commercial vocational schools, railway colleges, medical vocational schools, industrial vocational schools, and Hui Muslim middle schools. The Inner Mongolia Military and Political Academy had two thousand students. In addition, there was the North China United University (a merger of Yan'an University, Lu Xun Academy of Art, Foreign Languages, and Education Academy), with an unknown number of students. When the Communist army withdrew, the students of these secondary and higher schools automatically or were forced to withdraw with the army. According to Secretary Wang of the Twelfth War Zone Commander's Office, about 6,000 students withdrew with the Communist army, of whom 800 were shot on the road for being ideologically unsound. Some have now returned one after another. The Communist Party's Jin-Cha-Ji Daily was published the day before the retreat, and before leaving, one of the three large rotary machines left in North China by the Japanese was destroyed into scrap iron. The Struggle Daily of Gui Sui published a Zhangjiakou edition three days ago.

Generals Are Humble

In Zhangjiakou, we met Generals Fu Zuoyi and Dong Qiwu, who were both wearing grass-green military uniforms that were exactly the same as the soldiers. They did not take victory as glory and were very humble. Commander Fu hoped that the reporters would contact anyone at will to know the real situation of Zhangjiakou before and after. Mr. Wang Mingde, Secretary-General of Commander Fu, accompanied the reporters for half a day. He said: The spirit of the officers and soldiers of the Twelfth War Zone is "Although the treatment is different, the life must be consistent." Small kitchens are not allowed, and officers and soldiers are completely consistent in clothing, food, housing, and transportation. The reporter did not see any difference either.
