The Melancholy of Guangxi Women

— Eleventh Dispatch From Guilin, Our Reporter Liang Xiaozhong

The most mysterious situation of "adopting sons-in-law" among the girls in the Zuojiang River area is that, for the sake of life, many women often take a fancy to some lonely strangers, and then bring them into their homes, entrusting themselves to their service (naturally, these women have already accumulated a lot of money from their labor). Occasionally, the husband misses his hometown and wants to return for a visit, which leads to the story of "releasing the thunder." The wife will try her best to provide her husband with unlimited generosity to "return in glory," but strictly instructs him on the date of return. If he returns to his wife's house on schedule, naturally nothing will happen. If he overstays his return date, nine out of ten times his belly will swell and he will pass away. These fragrant and terrifying legends still circulate in Guangxi, becoming excellent material for unofficial history.

The Yao girls of the remote southern country grow up in the Garden of Eden of song, dance, and love. Singing is their spring. Their sweet dreams, the secluded forests and streams in the thousands of valleys, the grassy riverbanks with a view of a thousand feet on the plains, are filled with different languages and loud singing, so gentle, pure, and lovely. The women in the vast mountain villages of southeastern Guilin have always passionately worshiped a singing goddess, believing in the myth of her singing voice. It is said that the name of the singing fairy is Liu Sanjie, a native of Longshan Township, Guixian County, on the banks of the Yujiang River (her name, like the nationally renowned ethnic hero Wing King Shi Dakai, is deeply imprinted in the hearts of the people of Guixian County, taken as supreme glory). This beautiful farm girl loved to sing mountain songs from birth. Whether it was herding cattle, planting rice, weeding fields, cutting thatch... her charming voice could be heard resonating in the quiet sky at any time. A song by the river, a few cries, intoxicated the strong young men, teased the youthful teenagers, and brought down the smile of the earth... However, an ugly fate brought her the bullying, torment, and jealousy of her sister-in-law, who was determined to kill this innocent little sister-in-law. So, one day, under the pretense of chopping firewood, she took Sanjie to a very steep mountain peak and then pushed her forward, thinking that she had ended Sanjie's life and singing. Who knew that just as Sanjie was falling in the air, she grabbed a thousand-year-old vine, swaying in the middle of the abyss, facing the rapidly rushing stream. Sanjie's singing rang out again: "Sister-in-law wants to harm Liu Sanjie, thanks to a thousand-year-old vine." As the song ended, a stone door on the cliff opened with a "ya" sound. Liu Sanjie took her singing and walked into the cave, becoming a singing fairy. The story is light and interesting. Liu Sanjie's soul lives forever in the hearts of the girls. Many people sing, "If you don't believe it, just look at Liu Sanjie, her singing should surpass the nine heavens." Singing not only surpasses the nine heavens, but also brings together the girls in the free mountain country. When the year is coming to an end and spring is approaching, when the plums are cold and the peaches are bright, occasionally there is an unprecedented program in the mountain village (such as the Spring Festival in agricultural factories, the Pangu Festival in the Yao area of ​​western Guilin, the Egg-Throwing Festival in the Wanggang area...). The men and women of the entire village are completely immersed in crazy song and dance. The bright moon shines on people, the flowing water sets the tune, and a gust of mountain wind sweeps across the plain. The wonderful love surrounds the deep pine forest. The woman sings, "The stars in the sky disappear and reappear, a Milky Way is cold and clear, if anyone can count the stars, I will fly into the sky with wings." The man answers, "The stars in the sky shine every night, it's not that I can't count them, I'm most afraid of counting to the end of the stars, and my darling won't walk the Milky Way." One sings, one responds, and Venus and Cupid's love arrows lightly pierce their hearts. When the moon sets and the crows cry, and the dawn urges people, many lovers have already taken each other's hands and stepped into the girl's father's house to make it clear, followed by a betrothal (the Yao people in southwestern Guilin want several cows and white rice, while the Yao area of ​​Dageng Mountain likes to have hundreds of pieces of white silver dollars. Speaking of the Yao area of ​​Dageng Mountain, there is still a "prince consort" of the Jinxiu Yao King, who was a popular figure in the former provincial government, but the reason why this prince consort was able to "marry the princess" was not because of singing but because of appeasement). Thus, thanks to the legacy of the singing fairy, another pair of lovers became a family. This is the spring of the Yao country, and also a page of poetry in the mountains.

However, the end of the tragicomedy is often that women suffer the most painful sacrifices. The war and famine of the past two years have devastated the body of Guangxi. More than six million women have suffered double the pain. Grass roots and tree bark have blocked their innocent singing voices. Hunger and poverty threaten the survival of their husbands and children. Many pure souls have sold their cheap bodies. Many bright pearls on the road have helplessly become other people's concubines. Infinite sorrow teaches them to shed endless tears like Lin Daiyu. Empty stomachs teach them to live a life more tragic than Zhao Wuniang. What happiness has the heavens bestowed on the women of Guangxi?

Important Generals Who Recovered Zhangjiakou (From Right to Left) (1) General Wang Mingde, Secretary-General of Commander Fu, (2) Commander Fu Zuoyi of the Twelfth War Zone, (3) General Dong Qiwu, Temporary Garrison Commander, (4) Zhou Jun, Chairman of the Temporary Political Affairs Committee. (Photo by Our Reporter Song Shaobai)

Visiting Chairman You Yongchang of the China Zhonghe Party

— Twelfth Dispatch From Guangzhou, Our Special Correspondent Liang Feng

The name "China Zhonghe Party" seems to have rarely been seen in the past. I believe many people feel a little unfamiliar with this party. Therefore, when local newspapers revealed the news of the Zhonghe Party leader's arrival in Guangzhou, citizens speculated in the streets: "Probably another new political party has emerged." Even reporters had the same feeling. So, on a crisp autumn afternoon, the reporter, with a curious mood, went to Room 715 of the New Asia Hotel to interview Mr. You Yongchang, the chairman of the party.

Mr. You is now sixty-one years old. His face is thin, with high cheekbones and sunken cheeks, sunken eyes and a prominent nose. The white hair on his head and the silver beard hanging from his lips are harmoniously matched. When he received the reporter, he always had a kind smile, giving people the feeling of talking to a kind elder.

The Shen, You, and Xian Surnames Were Originally One Family

Mr. You's surname was originally the "尢" character without the dot on top of the "于" character. Therefore, many people pronounce it differently. Some pronounce it as the "尤" character, and some pronounce it as the "汪" sound. The reporter first asked about this, and he explained the origin of the surname. He said that their ancestor was originally Shen. Later, after a rebellion, the Qiren were scattered and divided into the Shen, Xian, and You surnames. In fact, they are all one family. Their original home was Wuxi, Jiangsu. Later, the You surname settled in Shunde County, Guangdong. As for this "尢" character, it should be pronounced the same as "注," but everyone calls me Mr. You, so I have to be surnamed "尤." He only explained his surname and didn't mind explaining it for several minutes, which also shows that he is a talkative person.

The History of the Zhonghe Party Has Been Around for Sixty Years

The conversation turned to the main topic. Mr. You gave the following overview of the history and current situation of the Zhonghe Party in response to the reporter's questions:

"The Zhonghe Party was founded by my late father, You Lie, in the Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty. It was established on the nineteenth day of the third month of the Dingchou year, and its history has been around for sixty years. At that time, it was a political party organized separately with the same ideology as the late Premier Sun after the Xingzhonghui. Mr. Sun and Mr. You were born in the same year, started the uprising at the same time, and fled to Tokyo and the Americas at the same time to lobby for the revolution. At that time, the Qing government called the four major bandits of the revolution the Premier, my late father, and Mr. Chen Shaobai and Mr. Yang Heling. For decades, the Zhonghe Party was led by my late father, You Lie. After my late father passed away, comrades at home and abroad elected me to succeed him. There are currently about three million members, mostly overseas Chinese workers in various ports in the South Seas, but there are also many in the country. The provinces north of the Yangtze River account for about 300,000. Although a correct survey has not been conducted on the number of party members in Guangzhou, it is believed that it is always more than tens of thousands, because most of the Zhonghe Party members are 'hereditary,' so they will only increase and not decrease. At the beginning of the War of Resistance, I went to Qujiang, Guilin, and other places from Hong Kong to mobilize party members to participate in the work of resisting the war. There was a time when I lost contact with party members in various places due to the interruption of traffic. Now I am planning to re-investigate and implement the revitalization of party affairs. Currently, the Central Executive Committee is located in Kowloon, Hong Kong, and will soon be moved to Shanghai."

A Historic National Seal Will Be Presented to the Government

Mr. You spoke eloquently, seemingly becoming more and more excited as he spoke, with a very proud look on his face. Then, he said:

"I am here to inspect the party affairs of the Zhonghe Party in Guangzhou. Soon, I will accompany the national representatives with Zhonghe Party membership to Beijing to present the 'Long Live the Republic of China' national seal to the National Government at the National Congress. This national seal was engraved in the twenty-eighth year of Guangxu when the Premier and my late father decided on the national title 'Republic of China' in Tokyo. The seal is made of ivory, about one square inch in size, and is engraved with six seal characters 'Long Live the Republic of China,' with two lions on top, which is very delicate. On New Year's Day in 1901, the Zhonghe Party started using it at the first congress in Tokyo. Later, it was also used on Chairman Chiang's 51st birthday, but it has rarely been used since then."

The Delay in Presenting the National Seal Is in Accordance With Family Instructions

After he finished this paragraph, the reporter had some doubts. Since it is called the national seal, why was it not presented to the National Government earlier? His answer was this:

"My late father had long planned to present this seal to the Premier. The Premier said that this was a national treasure and instructed my late father to hand it over only when the national revolution was completed and the National Congress was convened. In the 25th year of the Republic of China, the central government telegraphed my late father to Beijing to discuss national affairs, and my late father planned to present it to the National Congress at that time to show solemnity. However, later, due to the serious national crisis, the National Congress was suspended, and my late father unfortunately passed away in the capital. Before he passed away, he instructed me to present it at the opening of the National Congress, so it has been kept until now!"

Finally, he said: "My late father was a founding hero, and his revolutionary achievements are outstanding. He was selfless and dedicated his life to public service, and lived a simple life with noble ambitions. He was very friendly with Mr. Zou Haibin, Mr. Ju Juesheng, and Mr. Dai Jitao. After his death, he was publicly buried in Beijing, and friends founded You Lie Memorial Middle School in Hong Kong. The school's name was inscribed by Chairman Chiang. Currently, Guangdong comrades also have the intention of establishing a branch school here, and I also feel that cultivating talents during the period of national construction is the current urgent task!"

When he said this with emotion, the reporter still wanted to ask questions, but Mr. You had other social engagements, so the reporter had to leave.

Ten-Character Claim for Opinions on the Current Situation

Finally, I would like to report one thing here. The Zhonghe Party will issue a letter to Chairman Chiang of the National Government on the current situation on September 9 of this year. Although the content has not been published, the party has publicly issued ten major claims on the current political views, with the content being the supremacy of the country and nation, the primacy of recovery and construction, the immediate cessation of the civil war, and sincere cooperation towards the nation.

International Knowledge Published Every Wednesday

The Danube River Has Many Troubles The Struggle Between the United States and the Soviet Union Over Navigation Rights Affects European Peace

The United States has recently been fighting for an issue vital to European peace in two international conferences: the unrestricted use of the 1,750-mile-long Danube River for international trade. At the Paris Peace Conference, over Soviet opposition and after the United States withdrew its special proposals, a vague proposal to convene a special conference to internationalize the Danube River was passed. At the same time, at Lake Success, the United Nations Economic and Social Committee passed a similar U.S. proposal. But countries under Soviet control have vowed to refuse to attend any international conference that opposes their sole management of the Danube.

Therefore, this issue cannot help but arise again, making it difficult for the United Nations to deal with. The following is a dispatch from Vienna by Howard, the Berlin correspondent of U.S. Newsweek, detailing the various important factors behind this complex issue.

The Viennese have a witty satire based on Strauss's waltz, called "The United States Occupies the Vienna Woods, the Soviet Union Occupies the Blue Danube." The reason is that American officials and their families live in the stately houses in the "Vienna Woods" in the American occupation zone of Vienna, while the stretch of the Danube River and its tributaries from Enns in Upper Austria to the Black Sea is under Soviet control.

American Control of One-Fifth

— Translated by Zuo Xi

In reality, the United States controls one-fifth of the Danube River's total length, including a narrow upstream section from Ulm in Baden-Württemberg to Linz within the American occupation zone of Austria. From there, it extends along the southern bank to Enns, where the Soviets have placed underwater cables. In the river section above Linz, the Americans possess one-third of the Danube River fleet. This fleet comprises 971 vessels from Austria, Czechoslovakia, Yugoslavia, Hungary, France, Bulgaria, Romania, and other countries. These ships were used to transport retreating German expatriates and supplies during the final months of the war, or they fled upstream after the war to avoid capture by Soviet forces. Among them are 34 passenger ships, 105 tugboats, 55 motor barges and tankers. The rest are ordinary barges, oil barges, crane ships and other assorted vessels.

American engineers have cleared the river channel in Germany from Linz to Regensburg and have established three Danube shipping companies to manage navigation on a 296-mile stretch of the river within the American occupation zone. These three companies are the Bavarian Danube Shipping Company (DDSG), the Bavarian Lloyd Shipping Company, and the Comos Shipping Company, which is owned by Bavaria but chartered by the Netherlands. Of the 971 vessels, 390 are assets of the Danube Shipping Company. All the ships and other equipment of this company within the Soviet occupation zone were confiscated last winter by the Soviets as "German assets" under the Potsdam Agreement. Therefore, the company has requested that the Americans not allow the ships to sail until the issue of the Danube Shipping Company's sovereignty is resolved. The company demands that the Soviet side return the confiscated dock equipment and 220 vessels. Although the Austrian Parliament has nationalized the company, making it an asset of the Austrian government, the Soviet Union continues to occupy and operate these vessels and equipment under the name of the Danube Shipping Company.

The Blue Disappears

There is a Viennese saying that the Danube always appears blue in the eyes of a lover. But in fact, this putty-colored river that winds around Vienna like a dead snake shows no trace of blue. Seen from the sky, it resembles a flypaper, covered with dilapidated docks and warehouses, scattered with collapsed bridges, and the protruding hulls of various sunken ships. Viennese people like to gather along the riverbank, resting and reading under the trees, and even brave swimmers venture into this river. However, the stretch from Linz to below Vienna is entirely stagnant, foul-smelling water, with no ships sailing on it. The port of Vienna, with its ten-mile long docks and wharves, used to handle 1.7 million tons of shipping annually before the war, but now it is silted up and desolate.

According to the Soviets, the choke point of the Danube is the Tulln bridge, about fifteen miles from Vienna, which was destroyed by Hitler's guards. All five spans of the bridge are broken and submerged in the river. Recovering the Tulln bridge from the riverbed must be carried out in dangerous rapids and requires specially trained engineers, workers, and underwater equipment, all of which the Soviets lack. Austrian engineers estimate that, under normal conditions, with appropriate tools and labor, the bridge could be completely recovered in 30 to 40 days. However, the Soviets, using only one crane and a few Austrian workers, have only recovered one span of the bridge in nine months.

State of Stagnation

In the second week of July of this year, the Soviet Danube Shipping Headquarters in Budapest, Hungary, sent a circular to all shipping companies under Soviet control, announcing that the section of the Danube River from Vienna to the Black Sea was open for navigation. Companies only needed to give 24 hours' notice to confirm weather and river conditions and could freely use that section of the river. Only the Czech shipping company has accepted this Soviet proposal, in order to transport 2,000 tons of wood pulp from Bulgaria to Bratislava, Czech Republic.

Below Bratislava, the extent of navigational hazards, tariff regulations, border inspections, various taxes, and loading and unloading fees are unclear, and there are many restrictions. Even the extent of Soviet control is unknown.

There is no regular commercial transport on the Danube. Only about 300 ships operate in Bulgaria, Romania, and Yugoslavia, and about 30 to 50 operate in Hungary. However, due to the danger of mines and obstacles, transport is limited to one-way transactions and is extremely risky. British and American officials are well aware that the Soviets currently control the northern estuary leading to the Black Sea, but they admit that they know nothing about the situation at the other two estuaries and the Sulina branch to the Black Sea.

It is a very obvious fact that before World War II, the Danube was the trade artery of seven Central European countries, with a total of about 3,000 ships traveling to and fro, handling 3.5 million to 4 million tons of cargo annually. Now, however, it is in a state of stagnation. While Europe is looking forward to a peaceful resolution, these seven countries could have rebuilt their collapsed economies through Danube trade, but instead they are eking out a living on UN relief supplies and a small amount of freight.

News Dictionary

Potsdam

— Translated by Zuo Qi

After Germany surrendered in May 1945, the three major powers, Britain (Churchill and Attlee), the United States (Truman), and the Soviet Union (Stalin), held a meeting in Potsdam in July to lay the foundation for lasting world peace and discuss plans to intensify the war against Japan. On July 26, Churchill and Truman, with the consent of Chinese President Chiang Kai-shek, jointly issued the Potsdam Declaration. Within two weeks, Japan accepted the declaration and surrendered. As a result, the name "Potsdam" became famous worldwide and became a news term in newspapers.

Potsdam is located about eighteen miles southwest of Berlin, Germany, on the Havel River. The area is beautifully scenic and has historically been the site of German imperial residences, with magnificent buildings. The Potsdam Conference was held in the old imperial palace.

Earlier, there were reports that the three major powers would meet again in Potsdam to discuss intractable international disputes, but this did not materialize.

Recently, the American Association for Chinese Policy accused the government of having made secret agreements concerning China at the Potsdam Conference and demanded that they be announced, but the US State Department denied this.

Current Affairs Commentary

From Paris to New York, the Focus Remains on the US and the Soviet Union

— Chu Yu

The Paris Peace Conference has ended, and representatives from various countries have returned home. Paris, which was bustling for two months and eighteen days, has suddenly become quiet. The world's attention has also shifted from Paris to New York across the Atlantic. Not only is the United Nations General Assembly scheduled to open in New York on the 23rd of this month, but the Council of Foreign Ministers is also scheduled to meet in New York on the 4th of next month. The United States is currently experiencing a meat shortage, and the general public "has no meat to eat." Now that a large number of international dignitaries are arriving, the US authorities must do their best to entertain them with fine cuisine, making the shortage even more severe.

Peace Is Not Easy to Achieve

If we close our eyes and imagine for a moment, we can see that achieving world peace is not an easy task. The European war ended a year and a half ago, and the Pacific war ended more than a year ago, but true peace has not yet arrived in the world. Politicians and diplomats from various countries are working hard for peace, holding one international conference after another, trying their best to restore the post-war world to normalcy as soon as possible, so that all countries can share peace and no longer face the threat of wars of aggression. However, after a year and a half of effort, only draft peace treaties with Italy, Romania, Hungary, Bulgaria, and Finland have been completed, while other important issues, because the Council of Foreign Ministers failed to resolve them, were transferred to the Paris Peace Conference for discussion. The Paris Peace Conference failed to resolve them, and now they have been transferred back to the Council of Foreign Ministers. This is like going around in a big circle, returning to the original starting point. The problems themselves remain as they were, without any resolution. The people of the world, having suffered the great calamity of this war, have learned from their pain and are eagerly seeking peace. As long as there is a ray of hope, they hope that it will suddenly become clear. At first, they placed all their hopes on the Council of Foreign Ministers, but after disillusionment, they placed their hopes on the Paris Peace Conference. Now the Paris Peace Conference has again made the world feel the sadness of disillusionment. However, the world's hopes are now shifting to the United Nations General Assembly, and even the future Council of Foreign Ministers.

The world's attention shifts with hope, but where is peace after all? It remains an impenetrable riddle.

An Episode at the End of the Conference

The final meeting of the Paris Peace Conference was presided over by Guo Taiqi, the acting head of the Chinese delegation, who praised the conference and hoped that all countries would eliminate their prejudices and work for peace. US Secretary of State Byrnes also said, "Countries should recognize each other. No country can win a war alone, nor can it achieve peace alone in peacetime. Countries must work together to benefit humanity." Afterwards, British Foreign Secretary Bevin and Soviet Foreign Minister Molotov also delivered speeches successively, and finally, French Foreign Minister Bidault gave the closing speech. The conference thus came to an end. However, the representative of Yugoslavia was not seen at the meeting that day. According to a letter he sent to Guo Taiqi, the chairman of the final session, Yugoslavia did not approve of the peace treaty with Italy passed by the conference and had decided to withdraw from the conference. The achievements of the Paris Peace Conference were already mediocre enough, and to expose such a major weakness at the end is truly disheartening.

The Focus Remains on the US and the Soviet Union

The United Nations General Assembly has decided to open as scheduled, and the Council of Foreign Ministers will also be held in New York. Therefore, everyone wants to ask: will there be good results? Our answer is: "The key to success or failure still lies in the relationship between the US and the Soviet Union." Therefore, the world pays special attention to the speech delivered by Byrnes on the 18th. The content of the speech includes the following points: (1) The American people are willing to extend a hand of friendship to the Soviet Union; (2) Rumors that the United States has adopted a policy of containment toward the Soviet Union are entirely based on fantasy; (3) Promoting understanding between the US and the Soviet Union is the most difficult task facing politicians and diplomats today; (4) The United States will continue to oppose policies of individual alliances; (5) The most worrying aspect of the current international situation is that the relationship between the US and the Soviet Union has reached an impasse.

Byrnes's words were not only fully agreed upon by President Truman, but even his political opponent Wallace expressed satisfaction, believing that Byrnes had made progress, but still hoped that he would continue to make progress. Senator Vandenberg's speech also supported Byrnes's policy, saying, "Neither the Soviet Union nor the United States wants war. I hope everyone will stop talking about war. The foreign policy of the United States is a policy of peace, and it will succeed if it is not undermined domestically."

Trade Conference Held in England

The international trade and employment conference initiated by the United States began its preparatory meetings in London on the 15th, discussing the US proposals. Representatives from nineteen countries attended, but the Soviet Union did not participate. US representative Wilcox put forward five basic principles for the revival of the world economy: (1) Substantially reduce tariff barriers; (2) Countries should exchange goods with each other; (3) No country should discriminate against imported goods; (4) Countries should maintain a high level of employment; (5) All countries should be equal in the international market.

If we study the real motive behind the US's initiation of this conference, it is to restore freedom to post-war international trade. In principle, this is agreed upon by all countries; but in reality, there are still difficulties. First, the non-participation of the Soviet Union inevitably makes the scope of so-called international trade too narrow. Second, Britain and France cannot temporarily abolish their restrictions on imported goods. Third, economically backward countries must adopt "moderate protection" in order to implement industrialization. Fourth, the US's advocacy of the international free trade movement inevitably carries the color of economic imperialism.

Belgian Foreign Minister Spaak: A Key Mediator Between Large and Small Countries

— Translated by Jia Nan from "World Report Magazine"

Belgian Foreign Minister Spaak is now an important mediator between large and small countries. He will once again serve as chairman when the United Nations General Assembly meets in New York on October 23. The working principle of this socialist politician is to be realistic and pragmatic. In his youth, he was an agitator of social movements and had smashed the windows of conservative newspapers, but age and a sense of responsibility gradually turned him into a rational person who advocated reason. For example, at the Paris Peace Conference, Australian Foreign Minister Evatt used direct language to force the four powers to make concessions, but Spaak used gentle language and compromise methods.

The great powers resolutely rejected Evatt's demand that a majority resolution should be binding on the four powers. But when Spaak, as chairman of the rules committee, suggested that the great powers should automatically adopt proposals passed by a two-thirds majority, he won the support of US Secretary of State Byrnes.

When Spaak serves as chairman of international conferences, he is calm and accurate, truly representing the typical figure of objectivity and impartiality. He represented Belgium in international tennis competitions in 1922, and his flexibility and quick-wittedness on the court can be compared to his eloquence at the conference table.

Tactful Approach

When Spaak is chairman, debates rarely become deadlocked. In situations where the four powers face a stalemate, the Belgian Foreign Minister can often propose a tactful approach.

At the Paris Peace Conference, Spaak once told the representatives of various countries that their endless disputes would make people in the world think that they were not setting the terms for the Axis powers, but arguing about peace among themselves.

When Spaak is chairman, he never allows any representative to take advantage of the rules. In handling conference work, he attaches more importance to the spirit of the rules than to the letter of the rules. When there is a mistake due to confusion in the meeting, his attitude is tolerant, but if someone deliberately violates the rules to achieve their own advantageous purpose, his attitude is extremely firm.

In his youth, Spaak led socialists to parade and smash the windows of right-wing newspapers. In his twenties, he was an excellent lawyer and first attracted attention. He defended communists and wrote fiery pamphlets and speeches for young socialists. But when he became Prime Minister of Belgium at the age of 39, he was already the leader of the right wing of the Socialist Party and an opponent of the Communist Party.

Outstanding Talent

Spaak is the son of Belgium's first famous female socialist member of parliament. His father was a poet who wrote the most successful play of the time. In 1938, he became Prime Minister of Belgium.

During World War II, Spaak fled to France and was detained by the Vichy government. He then fled to Spain and was detained by Franco. He escaped from prison, disguised as a monk, passed through Portugal, and arrived in London, rejoining the Belgian government.

Spaak was first elected to parliament in 1932 and became a cabinet minister in 1935, serving as foreign minister the following year. Since then, he has held this position almost continuously. He is now the foreign minister of the coalition government of the Liberal, Socialist, and Communist parties.

In 1937, Spaak participated in King Leopold's negotiations, which resulted in Belgium breaking away from its military alliance with France and Britain. But isolationism did not save Belgium from aggression, just as neutrality did not save Belgium from crisis in the First World War.

But Spaak differed from King Leopold in that he fled abroad to continue the resistance. Today, he opposes Leopold's surrender to the Nazis and does not approve of his return to the country. Spaak now advocates close relations with Britain and France and the establishment of a joint defense agreement, but he insists that this is not the organization of a "Western bloc."

This policy has led the Soviet Union to oppose him serving as chairman of the United Nations General Assembly. But after seeing Spaak's actual actions, the Soviet side had to admit that he was an excellent chairman.

When the United Nations General Assembly meets in New York on October 23, he will once again appear before the representatives of various countries as a mediator between large and small countries.

Reasons for Japan's Defeat: Japanese Journalist Kato Reveals the Truth About Japan Before Surrender

A recent book by famous Japanese journalist and current chief editor of Kyodo News, Kato, titled "Record of Defeat," has been published. It states that even before the atomic bombs fell on Japan, American submarines had already dealt Japan a significant blow. A month before the atomic bombing of Hiroshima, Emperor Hirohito wanted to seek peace through the Soviet Union. Before that, Japan had repeatedly probed China for peace. Kato writes his article in the style of ordinary news reporting, beginning with: "Japan was already struggling in the throes of death. The sudden arrival of the first atomic bomb on Hiroshima was only the final blow that hastened its demise. The world's newest and most powerful weapon emerged from the summer sky and destroyed the city with just one blow, but its appearance did not have a major impact on the outcome of the Japanese-American War."

Kato appeals to United Nations readers about the mistakes of Japanese totalitarianism. He recounts the mutual suspicion between the Japanese army, navy, and civilians, the mismanagement of skilled Japanese workers, and the poor planning in all aspects of the war. He also harshly criticizes the ridiculous posture of the Japanese army pretending to be calm and covering up the truth when Japan was on the verge of collapse. He further describes the enslaved state of the Japanese newspapers, which were at a loss when they finally regained their freedom.

At the historic meeting held by the cabinet and other leaders on August 14, the Prime Minister first reviewed the general situation, after which the Chiefs of Staff of the Army and Navy, as well as the Minister of the Army, appealed to the Emperor to reaffirm the national policy and continue the war. At this point, the Cabinet Secretary quoted the Emperor as saying, "If others have no opinions to express, we will express our opinions. We are determined to have you agree to this... We believe that there is only one way left to save Japan."

Kato criticizes the propaganda on both the Japanese and American sides, saying: "In my personal opinion, Japan's propaganda in the Philippines was the most unsuccessful, while its propaganda in Burma was the most successful. The main reason for the success was the racial appeal and promises. The failure was due to the inability to replace the Anglo-American trend and the inability or unwillingness to fulfill promises. Especially in the Philippines, with the sudden cessation of the supply of American cars, refrigerators, and modern equipment, the natives quickly lost confidence in the Japanese's empty talk of co-prosperity."

The Artery of the Balkans: The Danube

Page 11

Spring and Autumn

George Bernard Shaw

— Zhang Yinhuai

Shaw is ninety years old. July 26 was his birthday. George Bernard Shaw did not like celebrating birthdays, and twenty years ago he swore that he would not celebrate a second one. That was in 1926, when he wrote: "For all these praises of me, I can receive them with pride. Only this is my first birthday celebration, and also the last one I plan to celebrate." For this reason, his friends: HG Wells, Professor Murray, Mansfield, Priestley, A. Huxley, and Xiong Shiyi, etc., each wrote a memorial or research article, compiled into a special collection to show their respect and love.

This old man is not really old. Although he is an antique of the modern literary world who has been with Victorian writers and experienced two world wars, few people feel the burden of his age. People only think that he is a great writer of this century, who has written two modern masterpieces: "Saint Joan" and "Man and Superman"; but they do not know that most of his life has become history. Among the writers of his generation were Kipling, Hardy, and Wilde. And when his first play (Rhinegold) was published, Tennyson and Browning were still alive.

George Bernard Shaw was born in Dublin, Ireland. His father was a humorous drunkard; his mother was a very accomplished singer. The family was poor, so he spent the first thirty years of his life in poverty. Throughout his life, he was a wise man who had not received much formal education; but he had read almost all the famous works on the planet. He loved music because his mother was a very accomplished musician, allowing the children to grow up listening to the music of Beethoven and Handel from an early age.

Shaw (Oil Painting)

— Clare Winsten

In 1876, Shaw moved to London with his family. He tried to write over a thousand words every day, and after ten years of hard work, he completed five novels and hundreds of short essays, but only sold them for a total of six pounds. During those years, he relied on his mother to make a living, thereby obtaining the leisure time to write.

From the age of twenty-six, he became a vegetarian—partly for humanitarian reasons, and partly for health. He despised meat-eaters. It is said that once, he and the meat-loving sculptor Rodin mocked each other because of this. Shaw was not only an ascetic in terms of appetite, but also an ascetic in terms of sexual desire. He was a Puritan. Although he had a playful epistolary romance with the famous actress Ellen Terry at the time, she always faithfully loved his wife, who had passed away three years ago.

In 1884, Shaw joined the Fabian Society, which had been founded only a year before, and enthusiastically promoted the socialist movement in the streets. Three years later, he shifted his focus from the working class to intellectuals, and his sharp and quick eloquence conquered many people.

Shaw was not only a social critic, but also an authority in the music and drama criticism circles. He wrote drama reviews for three years for "Saturday Review," which was edited by his friend Harris. This was a high-end publication in London at the time, and Shaw's position in the literary world had already been firmly established due to his sharp and witty writing style.

George Bernard Shaw's humor and wit are known throughout the world, and everyone regards him as a playful jester. In fact, he is an idealist wearing a clown's mask. He himself considers himself a prophet of the times, but whether this is the case will have to be left to time to make the final judgment.

However, his cold satire and hot sarcasm are only superficial forms, temporary tools—this is true. He himself once said: "If I didn't say it with a laugh, I'm afraid no one would be able to stand it." Beneath this mask of satire is an Irishman's passionate heart, a strong love for humanity, and broad sympathy. He always tries to improve the situation of the working poor, and often pays out of his own pocket to help them. As Chesterton said: Comedians are often the most serious people in the world. In public, he is certainly sharp-tongued and likes to mix laughter and ridicule; in private life, he is a quiet, friendly, and gentle gentleman.

Shaw has now established a brilliant position in literary history, and people often compare him to Shakespeare. (Shakespeare is one of the people he admires most.) Along with honor comes wealth, of course. Plays have brought Shaw a great deal of money. For many years, he was the highest-paid playwright in the world; recently, he has become the highest-paid screenwriter for film. Films based on his plays have to pay him one-tenth of the total revenue. The films that have already been made include "Pygmalion" and "Major Barbara," and the new film "Caesar and Cleopatra" has recently been completed. Therefore, when the British side wanted to award him the highest honor, he simply refused; he believed that the name George Bernard Shaw no longer needed unnecessary embellishments.

Shaw's important plays include the following: "Arms and the Man" (first performed in 1894). "Candida" (1894). "The Devil's Disciple" (1897). "Caesar and Cleopatra" (1898). "Man and Superman" (1903), first performed in May 1905. "Major Barbara" (November 1905). Later, he also wrote "Pygmalion" and his last famous play "Saint Joan" (1923), as well as many famous works on economics. It is said that he is still writing a play even now.

Anecdotes about Shaw

— Huai

George Bernard Shaw's humor is world-renowned. Once, a beautiful actress (not the dancer Duncan) wrote to him to propose marriage. She said: "Your brain plus my figure, we will produce the perfect child." But Shaw replied: "What if that child inherits my figure and your brain?"

Humor is humor, but most scholars, although they admire Shaw's intellectual enlightenment, do not appreciate his clownish face. He himself is among these people. One evening, after a performance of "Arms and the Man," Shaw was invited to take a bow as the author. At the end of a burst of enthusiastic applause, there was a sudden cold "boo." Shaw raised both hands to calm the frenzied crowd. Then he turned around to face the direction of the boos and said: "I agree with you, my friend. But the opinion of everyone in the room is exactly the opposite of ours. What can the two of us do?"

In 1925, he refused the Nobel Prize in Literature. His reason for refusing was very interesting: he did not need the money. The money was worth about US$35,000. He said: "Like a lifebuoy to a swimmer who has already safely reached the shore, it is useless."

Statue of Shaw by Clare Winsten

Right picture: On October 9th of this year, George Bernard Shaw fell off a swivel chair and had a fall, so he had to lie in bed and rest for a few days.

— United Press Photo

Shaw's Daily Life

— Lin

George Bernard Shaw has a three-story villa in Ayot, St. Lawrence, with twelve comfortable rooms. The garden occupies an area of one hundred acres. He lives a peaceful and leisurely life here, spending his time writing. He does not smoke or eat meat. He eats breakfast at nine o'clock every morning and reads newspapers—from the conservative "London Times" to the communist "Daily Worker." Then he hides in his work hut and writes until one o'clock. He takes a nap after lunch; around four o'clock, he returns to the hut. He stays there until seven o'clock for dinner. In the evening, he reads books and listens to the radio, and goes to sleep at eleven o'clock.

His wife, Charlotte Payne-Townshend, passed away three years ago. Now he lives alone in Ayot, hiring a driver, gardener, housekeeper, and maid. Every July, he must go to London to live for a while, so that the servants can have a rest, and the chimneys, etc., can be cleaned once.

Congratulatory Message on Shaw's Birthday

— Written by Professor Murray, Translated by Lan Ning

I am sick, but I cannot leave out GBS, whom I admire so much, from the group of commemorators.

Let me repeat an old inscription. In my book on Aristophanes, I wrote: "Dedicated to my old friend GBS, a lover of ideals, a hater of cruelty, a man who has filled the world with laughter, and whose courage never disappears—"

"A lover of ideals," although I have been with many cultural workers, I doubt that there are few who live such a strong spiritual life and rarely care about the physical aspects like him. He takes the enjoyment of food surprisingly lightly. Vulgarity and carnality are not found in his overflowing wit. Even trauma does not seem to disturb him much. Once, he was seriously injured, bandaged all over, with broken bones, and bleeding a lot. I went to see him, always thinking he was lying in bed, but he told me he was on a high ground in the garden. I went in and didn't see anyone, but I could clearly hear bursts of laughter coming from behind a clump of holly trees. Following the sound, I found him. He did not notice my arrival, did not notice his own trauma, and was writing with his unbandaged hand, laughing happily out loud.

Even as a reformer, what interests him is also ideals. Although he faces and understands worldly affairs, I think his excitement is mainly not for sympathy for human suffering, but more for the absurdity and facilities that cause these sufferings. He reforms with ridicule and cold logic, rather than appealing to emotions.

Of course, one cannot forget his extreme "hatred of cruelty," hatred of cruelty to both humans and animals. He does not seem to belong to our meat-eating race. This race's main pleasure in life is what we call "sports," that is, "hunting," "shooting," and "fishing," often inflicting death and trauma on almost every living and sentient creature. Similarly, he hates the oppression of human nature; it is not that he particularly likes foxes in cities or poor people. It is just that he cannot bear to see them being treated harshly.

Praising him for "filling the world with laughter" is too easy to understand, but two points are worth noting. First, I doubt that there has ever been a greater intellectual and satirist in human history who never attacked or disliked private individuals. He would vehemently criticize behavior or facilities that he thought were cruel or unfair. However, it never involved private individuals. Like general second-rate satirists, or even great predecessors such as Voltaire and Aristophanes, he never thought of hurting others as they did. However, like these two, he has a great asset that many satirists lack: he has genuine respect and appreciation for masterpieces of poetry, painting, music, and drama. Among contemporary scholars, few have a deeper knowledge of Shakespeare studies than him. He always pays attention to contemporary geniuses (not envy or jealousy); he was delighted for Tolstoy, Ibsen, Maeterlinck, and Rodin. He tirelessly helps young British writers.

His "courage never disappears." I am not just referring to his fearless attack on all vested beliefs or facilities with privilege and authority. He attacked conservatism and excessive rhetoric, superstition and science, as long as he thought one of them was overbearing, he would attack it regardless of everything. He also has a rare asset: the courage of genius, or I might even call it the stubbornness of genius. I still remember when his first play was published, everyone thought it could not be put on stage. Theater managers said that he had a bit of dramatic talent; as long as he could change his obscure script, or find a writer with agile thinking who knew the situation of the theater to help him rewrite it, they might be quite worth performing. But twenty years later, he finally resolutely wrote a script that someone dared to perform—"Arms and the Man." It was immediately successful, and not long after, Shaw gained his current position and became Europe's most famous and widely read playwright.

In addition to all his amazing talents, he is one of the most kind and generous people. I will not call him the smartest person; his genius in practice is not constructive, but analytical. Once, in the "Saturday Review," he defended several of his own works and boldly wrote: "Who am I to be fair and impartial?" This is a frank defense. Assessing the factors in the dispute, carefully synthesizing and pointing out a proper path, this is not his job. Officials and rulers can do these. Shaw's job is to point out those things that are wrong but not known; sometimes even at the expense of exaggerated or biased writing, so that people face those things that they cannot see or do not want to see.

(Excerpted and translated from the preface to the George Bernard Shaw Ninetieth Birthday Commemorative Collection)

An Inch of Land, an Inch of Blood 70

— Ye Jingfeng

I never knew what it meant to be busy or tired, but in our Tongxian Temporary Action Headquarters office, to say nothing else, just looking at the staff coming in and out, reporting, commanding, dispatching; and listening to the ding-a-ling-ling sound of the telephone, and the faint, secret buzzing sound of the telegram machine coming from the next room, constantly ringing, the captain, holding the earphones in one hand, receiving telegrams in the other, issuing orders, and reading reports; all of this, etc., even if you just sat there and didn't interfere, just listened and watched, you would feel dizzy, confused, and your eyes and ears would be buzzing.

The head from Beiping is now in the Twelfth Regiment, and has taken the post of temporary chief of staff, in reality to monitor the puppet autonomous army, fearing that it will take excessive action. On the one hand, I am assisting the captain in the office, and on the other hand, I am still working with Tiger to carry out the external liaison work after the launch. This responsibility sounds easy and ordinary, but as long as you close your eyes and imagine, at that time, inside and outside the city, soldiers and horses are rushing, guns and cannons are shaking the sky, bullets are flying randomly, people are shouting, the entire city will turn into a pot of boiling water splashing everywhere, and you have to go back and forth in this chaotic boiling to manage the progress of all parties, receive and send reports, and make decisions; one wrong move, and you may even have to pull out a gun to fight. Thinking about it like this, our job is not very easy.

Tiger, like me, is wearing the "Security Team" uniform, the only difference is that he has a bald monk's head, while I still have a men's haircut. At this time, he was idly doing nothing in the office, dozing with one eye closed, the one eye he opened was probably to pay attention, fearing that he would be left behind when we went out. Because the captain often teased him, saying that he was too young, and when he started working, he was afraid that he would not be able to suppress people. Behind his back, however, he praised him as omnipotent.

When things are busy, time passes quickly, and in a flash it is more than three o'clock. The captain saw that everyone was a little sleepy, so he called the service staff, ordered a few bottles of wine, and took out some ready-made canned food, biscuits, and pastries, etc., to wake everyone up, and at the same time let everyone "have a drink" to celebrate the victory and success in advance. The first one to be alarmed was Tiger, and the one eye that was closed immediately opened.

There is also one thing about Tiger that should be reported here. Tiger has been much more silent since he came to Tongxian than before. In the past, he didn't often interject and speak in front of a large crowd, unless he felt that this sentence had to be said, then he would open his mouth; but when he was alone with me, he wasn't very silent either, and he was very trivial, somewhat like an old woman's nagging. These two days, however, he has changed a bit, even when he is with me, he doesn't speak; doesn't ask, doesn't answer; as if he has something big on his mind.

Yesterday was especially special. Early in the morning, he asked me for a hundred yuan, saying that he had met someone from near the village who was going home, and he wanted to ask that person to donate some money to his mother. This amount is quite large (in the past, the limit was one yuan for money, for haircuts, baths, and buying snacks); not to mention this, and at that time I proved that he was lying, because when he lies, his big round eyes will blink at least three or four times, this is foolproof. It wasn't that I couldn't immediately expose his bubble, but I was curious for a moment and wanted to see what he was up to.

He took the money, and immediately smiled, chatting about everything, forcing out some words to make me laugh; and asked me for two hours of leave (because in official matters, he is my assistant, and considered my subordinate, and he must ask me for leave to go out). I simply agreed very readily, only instructing him to go quickly and return quickly, and not to delay official business. I originally planned to secretly follow his line to see where he was going, but unfortunately, the captain found me to talk, and I didn't have time for a while, so Tiger slipped away. He did come back in less than two hours, and I was too lazy to ask further; because asking would be useless, knowing that he had already prepared a set of words to deal with me; then why bother?

These two days have been so busy, but I have always paid attention to his actions. In addition to being overly silent, he is also constantly blinking, as if he is thinking about something. Even at this time, in the office, although he is said to be sitting on a soft chair in the corner, resting with one eye closed, I don't think he is necessarily fast asleep, he must be planning something there.

Fragments Under a Dim Lamp

Happiness

Two things called "Happiness" that are not happy now.

Mayor's Cleverness

"Sometimes, Mayor Wu Guozhen uses extremely subtle methods to express his thoughts..."

I think the mayor didn't do it thoroughly enough. In addition to ordering his own punishment for violating traffic rules, he should also punish the traffic police who were biased in stopping him and then letting him go.

Injections

Traveling requires injections, otherwise you can't buy a boat ticket. Below is a survey form:

From Shanghai to Fujian: cholera, smallpox, plague;

To Tianjin: cholera, smallpox, typhoid;

To Ningbo and Hankou: cholera;

To Taiwan: smallpox, plague, typhoid;

To Guangdong: smallpox, plague;

In short, you have to get an injection for every step you take. I am an amateur, are these injections to prevent infectious diseases in the places you go? Or are you afraid that people will bring infectious diseases from Shanghai to those places?

The Way to Wealth

— S·S

Human Relationships and Worldly Wisdom

I don't know if God and humans are deliberately joking? Or is it to add many thrilling and bizarre patterns to this vast world? So, since the beginning of history, there have always been more poor people than rich people in any place; it is not surprising that there are more poor people, but the wonderful thing is that there are also a few rich and noble people dotted among them, so that the turbulent world, the poor people have a goal in life, a goal of climbing up; they climb all day, year after year, until they can't climb and lie down. Seeing the bustling crowds, the dust迷in the middle of the road, climbing up and falling down, falling down and climbing up again, pleasing to the eye, it's really beautiful!

After thousands of years of climbing, the poor have gradually gained some experience and insights. They have learned the climbing method that doubles their efforts. If you do this for a long time, you can take a breath, stretch your waist, wash away the mud, and be a proud person. You must not think of the humbleness and pity in front of other people's feet when you climb, you should remember that this climbing method is a dogma painstakingly left by generations of ancestors, and descendants must克紹箕表, promote and glorify it.

Poor people all have a sour smell on their bodies, which is the biggest obstacle when climbing in front of wealthy people; so you should have self-knowledge, despite the blue robe于装, you must look cheerful and welcoming, your conversation must be gentle and flattering, and yet not fall into clichés; for example, if you know that the master you are welcoming and flattering is a surviving Qing elder, a local gentry, then you should scold science and slander people's hearts while holding the water pipe and agreeing with his intentions, but you cannot over-deny science and people's hearts, because the old masters are very clear that this time the Japanese were indeed defeated by the atomic bomb; if your master is a person who believes that ancestors all immigrated from Europe or America, then you should boast about how magnificent the Alps are compared to the several earthen mounds in Northwest China, emphasizing how magnificent the Mississippi River is compared to the several mud ditches in Southeast China; in the midst of your conversation, if the master's son and daughter "John" and "Little Mary" are eating with rationed food boxes, this is another wonderful opportunity; you can start by praising how much foreign countries value and reasonably emphasize national nutrition, and then analyze the ignorance, poverty, and poverty we showed in this war, and finally draw the conclusion to depict the luxurious scene of people throwing surplus materials into the sea; you are barking and making gestures, shrugging your shoulders, and the masters must also shake their heads, smile and say nothing, and then, when he thinks for a while, pats you on the shoulder and says: "Brother, you are really understanding!" You must not panic, bow your head and listen, expressing that you have met Bole, and that you will die without regret, and are willing to listen to orders, or結草啣環!

And so on, if you happen to encounter a master who used to be a traitor, and is still sitting high above one person and millions of people in a certain place, you must not tell him: the news that a certain close friend who used to be in the same temple as him has been 明正典刑; if you have a master who started his fortune with "national crisis money," "victory money," and "receiving money," and escaped the Qing Dynasty by being good at dancing with long sleeves, you have to explain to him: 儻来之财,原是取之无伤廉惠的道理; if you encounter a master who has just climbed up not long ago, like you, you should express your understanding of his "climbing method" and kneel down, declaring "I was born with a cheap face and cannot reach the top," complimenting him for being able to扶披後進, truly a senior style, a kind-hearted intention; you have to follow their heels slowly and steadily, pat them gently and heavily in the处, then: the masters will regard you as a life-and-death friend, the 同华们 will treat you as a slave and dog talent, and a group below who are also following you and patting your ass will regard you as a "lifetime model," then you can be considered to have climbed a level.

After you have climbed up, although it is still far from the standard of great wealth, you may as well take a short rest and relax your 神抓 that has been climbing so exhausted; at this time, you can brag to the younger generation who are following your heels and climbing up, as well as to the friends who are struggling in the "climbing ranks"; to the former, you must put on a serious and solemn appearance to explain to them the精与与深微 of the "philosophy of climbing," and to the latter, you should宣掦 the logic of "Hu Shi is my friend," especially to introduce your past masters, explaining that these are all relatives, old friends,乡椊同年; they feel that your loud remarks are aggressive, but there is nothing they can do, and they still have to express that I am not as good as you, and respect you very much; in this way, you can gradually leave the circle of poverty. However, you still have to pay attention to the timing, looking for a richer master to獻往日身手,迎拍如儀,拍好就爬,爬上去再吹,吹得四面八方,翕然景從, and as a result, climb to the "celebrity" throne, you may as well steal some free time in your busy schedule and shout a few high-profile "wealth is like floating clouds to me," and hum a few low-profile "feeling the times and cherishing blessings," guaranteed to be sung in harmony by hundreds and leave a lasting fragrance for thousands of years!

The philosophy of "climbing" is like this, and I am willing to make it public. The vast world, the sea of suffering is boundless, there are too many poor people, turning back is the shore, willing to climb together and ascend to bliss together! Amitabha.

Fine Words

— Hong Guo

There are two kinds of property that must not be wasted at will; one is the body, and the other is time. The increase of knowledge and the success of the enterprise are all related to this!

Intelligence is a kind of thing that is often mixed with laziness.

Love and borrowing are two difficult problems in life (but as long as it is not abused, then have the courage to do it).

To be a strong person, not a weak person; the so-called strong is to be strong in being able to manage oneself, control oneself, and dominate oneself. And know; putting a maxim into practice is stronger than saying a hundred maxims.

Quasi-Foreigner

— Bi Jun

In a certain church university in Shanghai, among the more than nine hundred students, nine-tenths are Chinese, and one-tenth are foreign students. Among the nine-tenths of Chinese students, however, there are a few who speak foreign languages fluently, wear foreign clothes, and have foreign names, thus they are equivalent to Chinese people with foreign appearances. This kind of student, they are definitely not satisfied with being Chinese, but they claim to be Chinese!

Although Chinese people may not all know Chinese characters, in any case, Chinese people must be able to speak Chinese (unless they are mute). Especially in China's highest institutions of learning, it is truly shameful to find students who do not know their own national language. This group of Chinese students who cannot speak their own language are simply shameless. Originally, there was a "Chinese" course for freshmen in the school, but they, like the true foreign students, were exempted from taking it. Indeed, there is not much difference between them and foreigners; they speak foreign languages, look like foreigners, and some even have birth certificates from Madagascar, Codo... They were born in a foreign environment, speak foreign languages, are protected by foreigners, and the schools they attend are also controlled by foreigners. In school, they receive different treatment from Chinese students. If you happen to talk to them for a while, they will unabashedly tell you in a foreign language: "I am also Chinese."

They receive preferential treatment at school because the principals of the school are foreigners. They don't have to pay tuition, and they can eat without spending money. The expenses of these students with unclear nationalities are entirely made up for by the tuition fees of Chinese students. The fists of these semi-foreigners when they are excited are also received by Chinese students. They clearly look down on Chinese people, but they often express in words that they are Chinese!

Seeing that overseas Chinese schools are prohibited from teaching Chinese by the authorities, and that overseas Chinese are indignantly appealing, and seeing the slave nature of these "quasi-foreigners," it really makes me want to cry without tears and laugh without being amused!

International Oddities and News

King of Turtles

— Yu Qiang

Regardless of whether a profession is high or low, large or small, as long as it is managed properly, "every trade produces its master." There are two brothers in New York's Broadway—Al Gold and Stanton Gold—who have become rich by selling painted turtles, which can be said to be "masters" outside of the three hundred and sixty trades.

Eight years ago, the Gold brothers started this novel business. After several years of hard work, the business prospered, and they have become wholesalers of "hard-shelled products." Gift shops and dime stores all over the United States sell these novel little gadgets. In addition to the old store on Broadway, they have also added several branches in midtown Manhattan.

These "hard-shelled products" are turtles painted with various colors, about the size of a pocket watch, with an average price of forty-five cents each. Customers can choose a name or a few words to engrave on the turtle's back with indelible ink. Some people engrave the name of their girlfriend, some use it as a birthday or wedding gift, some use it for advertising or display, and some even use it for proposing marriage.

Hollywood star Bing Crosby ordered a batch of "hard-shelled products" for his four children. Shirley Temple, Deanna Durbin, and other Hollywood stars are all fond of this little gadget, and even the serious Charlie Chaplin could not "avoid the trend." Former British Prime Minister Chamberlain once ordered fifty turtles by mail and gave them to his grandchildren. The package for the turtles is a specially made box with ventilation holes, lined with damp moss.

There are many reasons to buy this slow-moving animal. Parents often buy two larger turtles to bring home and paint for their children. A week later, they buy a smaller one, and when the children are asleep at night, they put the small turtle with its "parents." The next morning, the children discover this "miracle" and shout with joy, saying that the little turtle was brought by "cranes."

Some people believe that turtles can bring good luck, so they buy one for "good luck." There are also some people who are too lazy to reply to letters and feel bad about it, so they send a turtle with the inscription: "My reply is as slow as this guy."

The Gold brothers' most sincere customer was a father with two children. He bought three turtles and made a fortune. He had the names of his two children engraved on two turtles respectively, and the name of his family's good friend Nana engraved on the other. Later, Nana visited his house and saw her "namesake." She was moved by the gesture of friendship and took out a sum of money to establish an education fund for the two children.

The Gold brothers have turtle farms in two towns in Louisiana. About 15,000 turtles are shipped to New York every week, all arranged in rows in boxes filled with moss, most of which come from Louisiana. After arriving in New York, the turtles are placed in large buckets, waiting to be "manufactured." The first step is to apply a layer of protective white paint on the turtle's shell. Then, the little things are picked up by the dozen with a yardstick, and a skilled female worker brushes them with a brush, and then puts them on a rack to dry. The next step is to apply a thick layer of enamel—red, yellow, and blue are the three most popular colors.

If the turtle is large, it is suitable for birthdays or weddings. After the turtle is selected, appropriate patterns are painted on its back with special pigments. The "finished" turtles are displayed in buckets partially filled with water—the water in the buckets is warm in winter to prevent hibernation, and cool in summer to "relieve the heat."

The Gold brothers sell a special turtle food containing dried ant eggs and dried flies, the former from Finland and the latter from Mexico.

The Gold brothers also sell another novel thing: small American alligators. However, the "King of Turtles" complained that alligators are not very docile, nor are they easy to obtain year-round, and they do not have much attractive magic. Therefore, from a business standpoint, the Gold brothers still prefer turtles.

News Figures

National Treasure, White-Haired Youth - The Humorous Mr. Wu Zhihui (Part 1)

— Jifeng

Everyone is familiar with this aloof and humorous Mr. Wu Zhihui. When senior government officials took office, he was a veteran supervisor, always giving a speech, with a few witty remarks interspersed in the solemnity. On the 15th of this month, Mr. Fang Zhi, the new chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters, was sworn in, and the officiating officer was none other than the 81-year-old Mr. Wu. Recently, Mr. Wu also presided over the Mandarin Promotion Committee in Shanghai. (See this newspaper on the 16th.)

Morality and Scholarship

Mr. Wu is a veteran of the Kuomintang, with morality and scholarship crowning his contemporaries. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek respects him as a "national treasure," Feng Yuxiang once called him a "white-haired youth," and Hu Shih praised him as "one of the great thinkers of the past three hundred years." He is extremely aloof, striving to restrain himself. Throughout his life, he has taken not being an official, not riding in rickshaws, and not using servants as his principles. When he was in Chongqing, he often wore old cloth clothes, carrying a cane, and walked to and fro on the road. The "anti-war house" where he lived had thin tiles and a bamboo frame. It was probably built with bamboo and mud. The furnishings were very simple, and the room could only accommodate a few people.

Name Changed to Jingheng

Mr. Wu was originally from Xueyanqiao, Wujin. When he was young, he went to Yanghu County (under Changzhou Prefecture) to take the children's examination. Because his accent sounded like a Wuxi person, the other candidates suspected that he was impersonating and beat him up. Therefore, Mr. Wu hated it extremely and identified himself as a Wuxi person for the rest of his life. In the seventeenth year of Guangxu, he passed the provincial examination. However, he was extremely opposed to feudal ideas. Once, when the Wu clan was compiling its genealogy, he did not approve of it and angrily overturned all the character plates, which caused great hatred from the clan leader and public relations. He had no choice but to escape from his hometown. In the twenty-fourth year of Guangxu, he served as the president of Nanyang Public School in Shanghai. Together with Yuan He Chen Xiaozhi, he agreed not to read thread-bound books again. He also believed that "lacking reverence and knowledge is not enough to bear the weight of the world," so he changed his name to Jingheng.

In the tenth year of the Republic of China, he served as the vice president of the Sino-French University in Lyon, leading a group of students abroad. One day, Mr. Wu found a pair of pants on the ship. He personally washed them clean and then issued a notice: "A pair of stinky pants was found on the ground and has been washed clean. Whose are they? Please claim them." Sometimes, when students threw melon seeds and nutshells everywhere, Mr. Wu also personally held a broom and swept them clean.

Vowed Not to Be an Official

In the thirteenth year of the Republic of China, he served as a central supervisory committee member and has been re-elected ever since. As a founding elder of the country, he is already the most veteran of the veterans. Also, because he vowed not to be an official, he does not hold any positions other than supervisory committee member, and he does not easily attend unless it is an important meeting. Therefore, he has also earned the title of "reclusive celebrity in the court." (To be continued)
